2.22         Tariffs are currently uniform across Viet Nam. Industrial consumers face a tariff schedule
that has average, peak and off-peak tariffs, with peak rates being well over double the off-peak rates.
Unfortunately, few, if any, of these customers have time of day metering, and therefore this tariff
schedule cannot be applied. The introduction of these meters, for appropriate consumers, will be an
important step in establishing a cost reflective tariff that will provide incentives for conservation of
energy at peak times. The ADB is funding a tariff study to assist in the development of an appropriate
tariff policy, based on appropriate financial and social objectives (see Annex 7).
2.23         The present tariff structure broadly reflects the differences in costs associated with voltage
level and type of consumer. Therefore, charges to industrial consumers are highest for those supplied
at 6 kV or below, and lowest for those supplied at voltages above 20 kV. There is a subsidy element
in the Residential category: consumers face a rising block tariff, with the lowest block (up to 150 kWh
per month) being priced at D450/kWh, and the highest block (above 250 kWh) priced at D800/kWh.
The tariffs to  commercial customers are substantially above anything paid by other consumers



-17-
(D900/kWh against D550/kWh for LV industrial consumers and D800/kWh for the higher-rate
residential consumers). It is likely that residential consumers will be contributing proportionately more
to the peak than commnercial consumers do, suggesting that this difference is not cost reflective. In
addition, there is a tariff schedule for foreign customers (both business and residential), with tariffs
above the estimated LRMC  of 7 USc/kWh.  The existence of "wholesale electricity vendors",
particularly in rural areas, who buy electricity from the power companies and resell it, metered through
submeters, to small customers, is quite prevalent. The prices the vendors charge are considerably
higher than the official tariffs, ranging as high as Dl,000/kWh. The number of submeters is quite
substantial and, in the case of PC3, by far higher than the total of all its customers. The high prices
charged suggest that the willingness-to-pay for electricity is well above current tariff levels.
2.24        The main reform required at present is an increase in the average rate of the tariff, to
reflect to consumers the true cost of electricity supply. To improve the accuracy of the price signals
sent through the tariffs, the Government should consider: (a) introduction of metering to allow peak and
off-peak tariffs to be charged to large consumers; (b) introduction of demand charges for larger
consumers; and (c) increasing the level of tariffs charged to residential consumers, at least for
consumption over the minimum block. so that the higher rates are at least equivalent to that charged to
comnmercial consumers. Agreement was reached at negotiations that the Borrower would, on an annual
basis, furnish to IDA a review of the policy and levels of its electricity tariffs, including proposed
adjustments to meet the objectives of the power development program, and thereafter implement
proposed adjustments taking into account IDA's comments.
F. Sector Strategy
Sector Reform and Restructuring
2.25        The Government is developing proposals to restructure the power sector to introduce the
flexibility and efficiency that will be needed if the rapid increase in demand is to be met. On January
1, 1995, the Governnent created the General Company of Electricity of Vietnam, by decree number
562/TTg, dated October 10, 1994, to manage the entire power sector, with MOE, henceforth, playing
a broad policy-making and oversight role. This General Company is an independent juridical entity
with the legal name of Electricity of Vietnam (EVN). The legal charter of EVN laying out the exact
scope of its responsibilities and the organizational boundaries of the power sector entities under it, is yet
to be defined. Tentative proposals envisage the creation of multiple independent accounting and legal
entities in the core operational areas of generation, transmission and distribution. The existing three
power companies would be unbundled, each company becoming a distribution company, owning and
operating the transmission and distribution systems at 110 kV and lower, as well as small generating
plant, 60 MW and below. Separate distribution companies would be created for power distribution in
Hanoi and HCMC. A Generation Group would be created which would own and control all the larger
generating plant, with a Transmission Group owning and operating all transmission systems at and
above 220 kV.
2.26        In November 1993, the Government issued a decree on Build-Operate-Transfer (BOT)
contracts, designed to facilitate the introduction of this style of project into Viet Nam. The particular
emphasis was on infrastructure, including power. The regulations, amongst other aspects, seek to



-18-
define the terms and conditions under which BOT companies can be established, the taxation that such
projects will attract, and a guarantee regarding conversion of local currency into foreign expenditure.
Several BOT proposals for power generation are currently under Government's consideration.
2.27       IDA would be assisting the Government in the identification of an appropriate long term
structure for the power sector under EVN through a Power Sector Reform and Restructuring study to
be conducted by ESMAP (para.4.3).  This technical assistance is designed to assist the Government
and EVN in making the transition from the existing power sector structure to the new structure. This
effort is based on the principles of: (a) improving the operational efficiency of the sector; (b)
commercialization and corporatization of the constituent operations to provide greater managerial and
financial autonomy; (c) developing an appropriate legal and regulatory framework that would allow for
greater enterprise autonomy and requisite government regulatory oversight; and (d) a financially viable
and open sector structure that allows for increased private involvement in financing sector expansion.
2.28       In addition, IDA and other donors are planning to assist the Vietnamese in institutional
strengthening of the power sector. Funds would be provided under Japanese Grant Facility to help in
power sector institutional strengthening (para. 4.19). This technical assistance would focus on the
development of appropriate organizational structures, adoption of commercial management practices,
budget and control systems, reporting procedures and information flows, under the reformed sector
structure. The ADB is proposing to finance a study to improve financial and accounting systems, and
a second on tariffs; SIDA of Sweden is planning a managerial training program. Agreement was
reached at negotiations that the Borrower would furnish to IDA for its review and comments: (a) the
findings of the ADB sponsored Accounting and Tariff studies; and (b) its proposals for the
implementation of the studies' recommendations, and thereafter implement said proposals taking into
account IDA's comments.
Lessons from Previous IDA Involvement
2.29       There have been no previous IDA operations in the power sector in Viet Nam. However,
IDA has very recently been involved in the resettlement process in its Highway Rehabilitation Project
and the lessons learned from this project in regard to defining project affected persons and the legal
framework for resettlement and compensation have been drawn upon in preparing the proposed project.
Lessons from other power projects that are pertinent to this project are: (a) the need for thorough
investigations in the preparation of technologically complex components. This project is technically
straightforward in as much as the technologies of the various components are fairly straightforward and
familiar to the Vietnamese; where more complex technology is involved (load dispatch centers) adequate
foreign consulting assistance has been and will be availed of; (b) the need for care in preparing the cost
estimates; adequate contingencies have been provided in the project; and (c) the need to strengthen the
implementation capabilities of the institutions. While the concerned Vietnamese institutions are
technically capable of implementing the project documents, they need considerable assistance in
preparing bidding documents, bid evaluations and progress reports. This has been taken care of by
providing expatriate consulting assistance for assisting the Vietnamese in managing each project
component.
Rationale for IDA's Involvement
2.30       The Bank's Energy Sector Investment and Policy Review for Viet Nam (Report No.
10842-VN), has been instrumental in identifying the issues and options facing the energy sector and in



-19-
assisting the Government in developing its first least-cost power development plan. Viet Nam's need for
investment in the power sector is large. While IDA could finance only a fraction of its investment
program, its participation in the sector would help catalyze funds from other bilateral and multilateral
sources. The Government is committed to reforming state enterprises and moving from centrally
planned to market-oriented mechanisms. For the power sector, this would involve a staged process of
transition; first strengthening the existing institutions, then commercializing and corporatizing them and
subsequently introducing reforms and a regulatory framework conducive to private sector participation.
IDA's assistance in this effort would make a major contribution to an orderly development of the
sector. Finally, involvement of IDA in the early stages of development is expected to have a significant
influence on the optimum use of limited resources in fostering efficiency and conservation and an
environmentally sustainable development.
2.31       The project is consistent with IDA's Country Assistance Strategy (Report No. 13545-VN,
September 26, 1994) which proposes working with the Government to continuously update its
development plan, taking account of changing economic conditions; to improve efficiency of electricity
utilization through proper pricing and conservation; and to strengthen power agencies through technical
assistance and training.
2.32       The policies and programs pursued by the Government in the power sector are in
compliance with IDA's policies and guidelines for commitment to efficiency improvement (including
demand-side management and energy conservation), sector reform and restructuring, moving towards
commercialization and corporatization, and encouraging private participation.



Chapter m
The Beneficiaries
A. The Beneficiaries
3.1        The beneficiaries of the proposed credit are: (a) the Ministry of Energy (MOE) for the
National Load Dispatch Center and the National Training Center; (b) Power Company No. 2 (PC2) for
HCMC distribution, the Southern Region Load Dispatch Center, the Southern Region Training Center
and the Ba Ria combined cycle project; and (c) Power Company No. 3 (PC3) for Hue and Nhatrang
distribution, the Central Region Load Dispatch Center, the Central Region Training Center, the 220kV
Krongbuk-Nhatrang line and Krongbuk and Nhatrang substatior,, and the 110 kV substations of
Nhatrang, Cau Do and Lien Tri.
B. Organization and Management
MIinisty of Energy
3.2        The Ministry of Energy (MOE) is responsible for the production, distribution and supply
of electricity and coal. The MOE discharges these responsibilities through several wholly-owned
subsidiaries (Chart 1) under its supervision: the Institutes of Mine and Energy, the PCs No. I (North),
No. 2 (South) and No. 3 (Central), the Power Investigation and Design Companies No. I (North) and
No. 2 (South), the Coal Cornpanies in Cam Pha, Hon Gai and Uong Bi, and the Power Construction
Companies Nos. 1, 2 and 3. Electricity production, distribution and supply is carried out through the
three PCs. Following the creation of EVN on January 1, 1995 (para. 1.21), all entities connected with
the power sector come under its management with MOE retaining a broad policy-making and oversight
role.
3.3        The EVN is currently engaged in drafting its charter that would lay out the exact scope of
its responsibilities and the organizational boundaries of the power sector entities under it (para. 1.21).
To the extent that these organizational changes will affect the implementation responsibilities for the
proposed project, it will be necessary for the Government to define its financial and operational
objectives for the member enterprises and discuss and agree with IDA on appropriate modifications to
the legal arrangements for the project (including appropriate financial and other conditionalities), both
for ensuring satisfactory implementation of the project and for monitoring the operations of the power
sector. Agreement was reached at negotiations that any organizational changes in the power sector, in
so far as they impact on the terms and conditions of the credit, would be discussed between IDA and
the Borrower.
Power Company No. 2
3.4        Organization. PC2 was established as a juridical entity in 1976 (Annex 4) as the "Power
Company of the South", succeeding the "General Department of Power". In 1981 under Resolution
No. 15-DL/TCCB3 its name was changed to Power Company No. 2. Like all SOEs, PC2 had to re-



-21-
register under Resolution No. 388-HDBT in 1991. Resolution No 147-TTG of April 7, 1993
reestablished PC2 with a Capital of Dong 3,831,204 million and PC2 registered under Registration
Certificate No 102618, dated April 23, 1993. PC2 is wholly owned by the Government, and in many
respects has the characteristics of a government department, reporting to the Government through the
MOE. PC2 operates its own bank accounts and can borrow both local and foreign funds. Foreign
borrowing, however, requires the approval of the Government through the State Bank of Viet Nam.
3.5        PC2, headquartered in HCMC, is responsible for power generation, transmission and
distribution throughout the south of the country. Its area of 19 provinces covers Lam Dong and Thuan
Hai in the north and reaches across the Mekong delta in the south, including the province of Minh Hai.
At the end of 1993, PC2 had an installed capacity of 1,358 MW, generating 4,661 Gwh. In 1993 it
had total sales of 3,646 Gwh and served a population of 25.6 million.
3.6        The organization of PC2 is structured along functional lines and is shown in Chart 2. It is
headed by a Director General assisted by four Deputy Directors General for: production, technical
matters, construction supervision, and economics; and a Chief Accountant. The Director General, the
Deputy Directors General and all officials responsible for an "account" (management of funds), i.e. the
heads of power stations and regional offices, are appointed by MOE, while department directors at
headquarters are appointed by the Director General. While PC2's organizational structure appears to
fulfill its current operational needs, it would need to be carefully reviewed in the light of prospective
reforms in the power sector.
3.7        On the whole, PC2's management and staff are technically competent. As of 1993, it had
a total staff of 11,180 of which 1,240 comprise engineers and other university level employees, 645
middle level employees, and 5,323 technicians. The rest are lower level semi-skilled workers. With a
staffing ratio of eight employees per installed MW, the company has the same ratio as for the Thai
power sector. By the end of 1993, PC2 had a total of 736,658 customers of which 655,722 were
classified as residential, 41,330 as industrial, 4,421 as agricultural, 34,475 as commercial and 710 as
"transport customers" (airports, etc.). In addition, there were a considerable number of sub-consumers.
PC2 has about 65 customers per staff which is low, when compared to a figure of about 120 for
Thailand. Significant improvements should be possible in PC2's performance figures over time.
3.8        Operation. Maintenance and Store Keeping.  PC2's operation and plant maintenance
standards and practices are satisfactory. With dramatic shortages of funds and very unreliable spare
part supplies, PC2 has maintained a reasonable standard of operational quality. Plant and warehouses
are meticulously kept and materials and supply are properly recorded. Major maintenance is done by
contractors while routine maintenance is done by company staff. Transmission lines are inspected
routinely and in accordance with fixed schedules. PC2's operations show technical and non-technical
losses of about 20% and 3%, respectively.
Power Company No. 3
3.9        Organization. PC3 was established in 1975 (Annex 4) following a takeover from the
French company of SIPEA. The legal basis, ownership and other institutional features of PC3 are
similar to those of PC2.
3.10       PC3, headquartered in Danang serves the central part of Viet Nam covering a total of 11
provinces, from Quang Binh to Dac Lac and Khanh Hoa, and serves a population of about 11 million.



-22-
At the end of 1993, PC3 had an installed capacity of 214 MW and had substantial power purchases
from PCI and PC2. With the exception of 20 MW in hydro power and 14 MW in gas turbines, PC3's
generating capacity consists of small diesel stations, mostly in isolated areas. In 1993 it generated 255
Gwh; imported 443 Gwh from PCI, 159 Gwh from PC2, and 3 Gwh from larang II, a small MOE-
owned hydro station.
3.11        Chart 3 shows PC3's organizational set-up which conforms with the other power
companies in Viet Nam. PC3's management and staff are technically competent. Of its total staff of
5,875 in 1993, 1,526 are engineers, other university level staff (accountants, computer specialists, etc.),
technicians and draftsmen, 540 are administrative staff, and 3,809 are lower level semi-skilled workers.
By the end of 1993, PC3 had a total of 158,000 customers of which about 6,350 were classified as
industrial, 920 as agricultural, 130,000 as domestic and about 20,730 as others. PC3 employs about 27
staff per MW and has 103 customers per staff. These figures compare unfavorably with those of PC2
and can only partially be explained by the small size and vastly outstretched nature of its operations.
Significant improvements should be possible in these performance figures over time.
3.12        PC3's supply area also includes a large number of "wholesale electricity vendors" or sub-
consumers, particularly in villages, who buy electricit) from PC3 for sale to small customers through
sub-meters. A study carried out by PC3 in 1993 indicated that in addition to PC3's 158,000 regular
customers, there were about 450,000 sub-consumers who pay much more'' than the official tariff
(para. 2.23).
3.13        Operation, Maintenance and Store Keeping.  PC3 conducts regular maintenance of its
plants and warehouses and properly records its supplies. Its transmission lines are inspected at regular
intervals.  However, while the standards observed for major maintenance are reasonable, further
improvements are possible.  Technical losses, including both transmission and generation losses,
amount to about 18% while non-technical losses are about 7% of electricity produced. PC3 would need
to exercise stricter control on its operations to reduce non-technical losses down to about 3 % as planned
by the Govermnent. Agreement was reached at negotiations that PC3 would prepare and implement an
action plan, satisfactory to IDA, for progressively reducing its non-technical losses to a level of 3%.
C. Staff Development and Training
3.14        The training centers of PC2 and PC3 were originally part of the Vietnamese educational
system.   While they are now  under the control of the PCs, they still operate as national
technical/vocational schools and are staffed and equipped for that role rather than for power sector
oriented training. Consequently, their efforts tend to focus on technical education, rather than on
training for the PCs' needs. PC2's training center is the Hocmon College which was built in 1960 and
operated until 1976 by the Education Ministry. The center's role is to provide initial training in power
plant and transmission/distribution for technicians and skilled electrical workers. The training facilities
I/ The sub-charges, which range from D 450 to D 1.000. is further broken down as follows: (a) 31% of sub-consumers paying
D 450 to D 550/kWh; (b) 50% of sub-consumers paying D 550 to D 800/kWh; and (c) 19% of sub-consumers paying D 800 to
D 1,000/kWh.



-23-
are poor and inadequate. The training courses, which are provided on request and tend to be of long
duration, seem to be as extensive as these limited facilities allow. PC3's training center in Hoi-An is
similar to that of other PC training centers in Viet Nam. Equipment for practical training is virtually
non-existent and the training network is inadequate.
3.15       The MOE and the PCs are committed to a program of major upgrading of staff skills,
which is essential if the PCs are able to manage new and sophisticated plants and systems. With
investments under the proposed project, the training departments of PC2 and PC3, would acquire the
capability and resources to supply the required training services (para. 4.13).
D. Billing and Collection
3.16       PC2 and PC3 operate a decentralized billing and collection system through their district
offices. The role of the head office consists of monitoring, collecting and processing of records through
a central computer arrangement where invoices are prepared. Billing and collection are undertaken on
a monthly basis for all customers. Meter readings are done manually and transferred to account cards
in each district office. Personal computers are routinely employed in the districts permitting the
transfer of information to headquarters through diskettes. The billing and collection policy of PC2 is
satisfactory (see Annex 5 for details). The collection performance of PC2 is relatively strong and
comparable with the performance of Thai utilities, holding arrears to about 52 days on average.
3.17       Because of the nature of PC3's market, its accounts receivables at the end of 1993 stood at
D385 billion, equal to about 464 days of sales. About D30 billion in arrears were mostly owned by the
agricultural sector. While PC3's policy is such that an account becomes past due after three months in
arrears, the Government allows them to write-off arrears by way of Government fund transfers. The
latest write-off was done in February 1994 when about D300 million was transferred to PC3 from the
budget. Some of PC3's accounts are not collectable, in particular, farners suffering from poor harvest
but who continue to be provided electricity, and for them, the Government has set aside funds for their
arrears. PC3 needs to bring down the level of its receivables considerably. Agreement was reached at
negotiations that PC3 will prepare and implement an action plan, satisfactory to IDA, to reduce its
receivables. On and after December 31, 1996, its net receivables (after provision for bad debts) should
not be more than four months of sales revenue.
E. Accounting System and Procedures
3.18       The present financial and accounting systems of PC2 and PC3 are inadequate. Prior to
1990, the power subsector operated under the accounting system of centrally-planned economies. In
1990, the system was abandoned and one based on the French accounting standards was introduced
countrywide. However, the modifications to the system, which were specifically aimed at tight
government control, resulted in an unusual accounting system with the following features:
(a)   separate books and accounts are maintained for the construction and operation functions of
the PCs; no consolidated accounts are kept that provide an overall financial picture;



-24-
(b)   official year-end financial statements are not produced and the accounts are not routinely
reconciled, casting doubt on their reliability;
(c)   cash flow statements are non-existent, making it difficult to assess the PCs' cash positions,
allocations of net income, and the extent of Government contributions by way of equity,
subsidies and grants. This information is particularly significant as unusual fund transfers
occur to the Govermnent, by way of regular depreciation charges, and from the
Government by way of budget allocations;
(d)   values of fixed assets are distorted. Upon unification of Viet Nam, the PCs' assets were
valued using standard unit prices, which was typical of the system used by many centrally-
planned economies. These asset values remained on the PCs' books at cost without regard
for the general development of the economy and inflation. After minor adjustments were
made in 1981, 1985 and 1989, a nationwide asset revaluation exercise was decreed in
1990 for all industries using the following parameters: (i) Ruble 1 = D2,400 for assets
procured from the formner Soviet Block; and (ii) US$1 = D2,400 for assets procured
abroad elsewhere. A second nationwide revaluation was undertaken in January 1992 using
the following rates of exchange: (i) Ruble 1 = D110,000 for all assets procured from the
former Soviet Block; and (ii) US$1 = D10,000 for assets procured abroad elsewhere.
Revaluing assets by equating the US dollar to the Russian Ruble is misleading, as the
value of the dollar in relation to the ruble at that time was US$1 = Ruble 100. In
summnary, because of the various accounting actions that have taken place in the valuation
of assets, it is not possible to state definitely whether the assets.are properly valued;
(e)   accounts are kept on a cash and not on an accrual basis;
(f)   depreciation is treated unconventionally, by separating depreciation into regular and
"Major Maintenance".  Currently, regular depreciation charges are remitted to the
Government in cash (except on assets financed by the PCs' own funds) while Major
Maintenance depreciation charges are retained by the PCs. In addition, there are no fixed
depreciation charges; the Government allows variations in the yearly depreciation rates in
order to adjust final financial results. The Government also permits the depreciation of
written-off assets. However, starting 1995, this requirement of separating and remitting
depreciation charges will be discontinued (para 5.9);
(g)   certain expense items such as staff bonuses, staff benefits and office maintenance,
normally recorded in the income statement, are booked as a cash outflow transaction. As
a result, net income is overstated by about 50% on average; and
(h)  land is not valued as only the Government can own land;
3.19       In the context of its upcoming Power Distribution Rehabilitation Project, ADB proposed to
finance a consulting study, "Improvement of Financial and Accounting Systems of the Power
Companies in Viet Nam" (Annex 6), aimed at introducing a modem accounting and management
information system. The Japanese Grant Facility is assisting in carrying out a study aimed at improving
and modernizing the conmmercial systems and institutional strengthening of the power sector (para.
4.19). These studies are crucial for assisting the Government in implementing the important aspects of
its Program of Economic Reforms, and for the PCs in introducing modem financial practices. The



-25-
ADB study is estimated to take about 10 months and should be available late in 1995 or early 1996
while the JGF-assisted study is expected to be completed by the end of 1995.
3.20       Until a major improvement in the accounting system is implemented, it is important to
introduce the following changes: (a) to provide an overall financial picture, consolidate the accounts of
both operation and construction divisions; (b) implement an accrual basis of accounting; (c) discontinue
the depreciation of written-off assets; (d) apply a single depreciation rate for normal depreciation
charges; (e) write off obsolete stock; (f) to reflect actual profits and losses, record all expense items in
the income statement, particularly those that apply to staff bonuses, staff benefits, and office
maintenance; and (g) make adequate annual provision for doubtful debts. Agreement was reached
during negotiations that PC2 and PC3 would introduce the above changes to the accounting system
starting with the financial year 1995.
F. Financial Management and Reporting
3.21       The management practices pursued in PC2 and PC3 are outdated. The existing reporting
system has evolved primarily in response to the Government's external reporting requirements and is
used by the Government for strict monitoring of the PCs. A functional management reporting system
would be difficult to implement despite the new accounting regulations introduced in 1991. A main
drawback of this system, as far as interpreting the financial statements of PC2 and PC3 is concerned, is
that the statements do not focus on financial performance; for example, it-is impossible to calculate a
rate of return on capital invested or any other meaningful operating ratio. The ADB and JGF-financed
studies (para. 3.19) will address this issue and should help the PCs introduce modem financial
practices.
3.22       The accounting staff of PC2 and PC3 are competent, and carry out their tasks of account
keeping and reporting in accordance with the requirements of the Government. The competence of the
accounting staff of both companies should considerably facilitate the introduction of accounting reforms.
The position of the Chief Financial Officer/Chief Accountant within higher management is either
unclear or does not receive due recognition in PC2 and PC3. In PC2, for instance, the incumbent is
subordinate to the Deputy Director of Economics, as far as accounting is concerned, but reports directly
to the Director General in its capacity as Chief Financial Officer. A similar structure exists in PC3.
The arrangement reportedly did not create problems in the past, because in a centrally-planned
economy, the financial activities of PC2 and PC3 were basically confined to bookkeeping, while
financial planning and investment finance were left to the Government as and when required. With the
expected rapid expansion of the power subsector and decentralized financial decision-making transferred
to PC2 and PC3, the position of Chief Financial Officer/Chief Accountant will be crucial, and will need
to be reviewed.
G. Taxes and Insurance
3.23        PC2 and PC3 are subject to the following major taxes: (a) tax on revenues (turnover tax),
levied at 8% of power sales (net of inter-PC sales), and 4%  on other revenues; (b) environmental



-26-
charge (royalty), levied at 2% on the use of water for hydro generation and calculated on the basis of
the PCs' share of revenues from power sales generated from hydro against total generation; (c) tax on
capital, levied at 2.4% of plant in service, less accumulated depreciation and assets financed from the
PCs' own funds, plus working capital; and (d) income tax on net profit, at the rate of 25% as of
September 1993, down from the 30% level of August 1993.
3.24       It has been the Government's practice to reduce the tax rates or even eliminate certain
taxes of PC2 and PC3 completely if the tax charge would result in unfavorable financial outcome for
these PCs.
3.25       In accordance with the general practice followed in Viet Nam, PC2 and PC3 do not carry
any insurance protection for buildings and their contents and for other assets. Nor do they carry any
third party liability insurance. Agreement was reached during negotiations that PC2 and PC3 would
make provisions, satisfactory to IDA, for insurance against such risks and in such amounts consistent
with appropriate practice.
H. The Budget Process
3.26       The existing budget process is designed to support applications by the PCs for funds from
the Government Budget and to provide the Government with a tool to exercise tight financial control.
The PCs' annual accounts at the close of the budget year are considered "closed" only when the
Government, through its auditing process, "approves" the accounts. The budget process also lacks
flexibility. For instance, at the beginning of the budget year, the PCs budget fuel expenses on the basis
of average hydrological conditions. However, should the availability of water during the dry season be
less favorable than anticipated, the shortfall has to be financed from the PCs' own resources, often
through expensive short-term borrowing from local banks, because additional budget funds are not
made available to them. The budget process would need to be critically reviewed under the proposed
Power Sector Institutional Strengthening study (para. 4.18).
I. Audit
3.27       There is no independent external audit of Government entities in Viet Nam. In 1991 the
Government considered establishing an "independent" audit process for SOEs and in the process created
the Viet Nam Auditing Company (VACO). VACO, with three offices in Hanoi, Ho Chi Minh City and
Danang, was created by Government Decree No. 165. TC/QD/TCCB on May 13, 1991. It was created
as a dependent body of the Ministry of Finance (MOF) and cannot therefore be considered an
independent auditing firm. However, in a joint venture with a reputable international firm, VACO
audits would be acceptable to IDA. The Govermnent has granted several foreign accounting firms
licenses to operate as independent auditors in Viet Nam. There are currently four independent auditing
firms operating in Viet Nam.
3.28       So far, the annual financial statements of PC2 and PC3, which are not published, have not
been audited by independent auditors and the PCs do not have internal auditing departments. Their



-27-
audits, however, are routinely audited by auditing teams of the MOF and MOE. This audit, which is
also used by the MOF to determine tax liabilities, is usually conducted within one month of submission
of the PCs' annual financial statements. In addition, Government staff carries out controls on special
problems. Realizing that a full conventional and commercial audit by the Government is difficult to
perform prior to upgrading the entire accounting system, and in order to assist PC2 and PC3 to
familiarize themselves with the principles of modem accounting systems, agreement was reached at
negotiations that the Borrower, PC2 and PC3 will appoint independent auditors acceptable to IDA. The
audit report would be made available to IDA within nine months after the close of each financial year.



Chapter IV
The Project
A. Objectives and Description
4.1        The main objectives of the proposed project are to: (a) assist the Government in
optimizing its investment decisions and help meet demand growth; (b) help improve the efficiency of
the power supply system by: (i) rehabilitating and reinforcing transmission and distribution systems; (ii)
converting generating plants from open to combined cycle operation; and (iii) installing modem load
dispatch centers; (c) strengthen the planning, administrative and management capabilities of the power
companies through technical assistance and training; (d) rationalize and strengthen the training systems
for the power sector; and (e) assist in the review of issues and options in the promotion of electricity
energy efficiency and demand side management. Also, in association with the project, the Bank's
ESMAP would be assisting the Government in examining the issues and options in reforming the power
sector through a study entitled "Power Sector Reform and Restructuring".
Project Description
4.2        The proposed project would finance priority investments in the power systems of Southern
and Central Viet Nam falling under the jurisdictions of PC2 and PC3, respectively. Its components
include: (a) for PC2: (i) rehabilitation and reinforcement of the distribution system in HCMC; (ii)
conversion of three 37.5 MW open cycle turbines to a 170 MW combined cycle unit at Ba Ria; (iii)
establishment of the Southern Region Load Dispatch Center; (iv) establishment of the Southern Region
Training Center; (v) resettlement and/or compensation of persons affected by components a (i) and a
(ii); and (vi) consulting services for detailed engineering, procurement and construction supervision, and
an engineering study for the Dai Ninh Hydropower project; (b) for PC3: (i) rehabilitation and
reinforcement of the distribution systems of the cities of Hue and Nhatrang; (ii) construction of the 220
kV Krongbuk-Nhatrang transmission line and 220 kV substations at Krongbuk and Nhatrang, and
expansion of the 110 kV substations at Nhatrang, Cau Do and Lien Tri; (iii) establishment of the
Central Region Load Dispatch Center; (iv) establishment of the Central Region Training Center; (v)
resettlement and/or compensation of persons affected by components b (i) and b (ii); and (vi) consulting
services for detailed engineering, procurement and construction supervision. The project also includes:
(a) for MOE: (i) expansion of the National Load Dispatch Center; (ii) procurement of equipment for the
National Training Center; and (iii) engineering studies for the Son La Hydropower project; and (b) for
the Power Sector: (i) technical assistance in strategic planning, MIS, human resource development,
financial management and materials managernent; and (ii) technical assistance in demand-side
management and electricity efficiency imnprovement.
4.3        The Power Sector Reform and Restructuring study by ESMAP (para. 4.18) would,
through seminars, workshops and study tours, focus attention of the Vietnamese on issues relevant to:
(a) improving the efficiency of technical and managerial operations; (b) commercialization and
corporatization leading to greater managerial and financial autonomy with accountability; (c) the legal
and regulatory framework for the sector; and (d) an industry structure that would facilitate private
financing of power development. The study's terms of reference are at Annex 8.



-29-
Description of The Project Components
Conversion of Open Cycle Combustion Turbines to Combined Cycle Operation at Ba Ria
4.4        The existing power station at Ba Ria in the south is provided with 5 Frame 6 combustion
turbines until recently burning diesel oil. Off-shore natural gas is expected to be available at Ba Ria in
mid-1995. While providing a more economical fuel source, natural gas opens up the possibility of
increasing generation at Ba Ria, without incremental fuel consumption, by converting the open cycle
turbines to combined cycle mode with the installation of the steam cycle equipment. To justify the
large per unit capital cost of US$1,300/kW of the steam cycle equipment, a detailed economic study,
considering power and energy balance in the southern grid, was conducted by consultants. This study
establishes the need for high plant factor thermal capacity addition in the southern grid and provides the
rationale for conversion to combined cycle operation at Ba Ria. A subsequent detailed technical
feasibility study by the same consultant establishes the technical parameters for the conversion of 3x37.5
MW combustion turbines to combined cycle operation by the installation of 3 heat recovery boilers and
a 57 MW steam turbine. The cooling source for the steam cycle is currently planned to be through the
creation of a pond in the nearby estuary. The economics of the alternative with land-based cooling
towers, which would eliminate the aquatic environmental impact, is under consideration by PC2. If the
cooling pond alternative is adopted, a part of a cooperative shrimp farm would need to be acquired and
suitable compensation paid (para. 4.29).
Rehabilitation/Reinforcement of the Distribution System of Ho Chi Minh City (HCMC)
4.5        HCMC is the industrial, scientific, technical and international relations center of Viet
Nam. Its metropolis, with 12 districts and an area of 140 sq km has a population of 3.2 million
(population density: 23,000 persons/sq km), whereas its suburbs, with 6 districts and an area of 1,916
sq km have a population of 1.4 million (population density: 7 persons/sq Ian). The MV and LV power
distribution systems in HCMC are operated by the Power Supply Department, a subsidiary of PC2,
while PC2 itself operates the HV transmission system and the HV/MV source substations. The demand
for electricity in 1993 was 420 MW, 2,352 Gwh p. a., with losses amounting to about 19% of which
about 3% are estimated to be non-technical. A recent detailed evaluation of the HCMC distribution
system concludes that: (a) many of the substations are overloaded, almost all of their equipment is old,
undermaintained due to lack of spares and poses serious operational problems and safety hazards; (b)
the overhead MV network, though in a reasonable physical condition, has almost half its circuits
overloaded, whereas the underground MV cables are over 40 years old and prone to frequent faults;
and (c) the LV overhead network is in a very bad condition and is in urgent need of rehabilitation.
4.6        A master plan study for the rehabilitation and expansion of the HCMC distribution system
was carried out by consultants. The Base Case load forecast scenario developed by the consultants,
based on an update of MOE's recent forecasts, indicates the demand growing from 510 MW and 2,869
Gwh in 1994 to 1,237 MW and 7,286 Gwh in 2000, reflecting an average growth rate of about 16%.
The study presents the investments in the short and medium term to rehabilitate and reinforce the
network (including upgrading MV and LV voltages and reconductoring), which would reduce its losses
from the current level of about 19% to about 10% by 2005. If these investments are not made, the
losses would increase tremendously, and system reliability would seriously deteriorate. The planning
basis is considered to be reasonable and practicable. The proposed project covers rehabilitation and
expansion of the MV and LV lines and MV/LV substations over the 1995-1997 period (see Annex 9,



-30-
page 2 for details). Provision has been made for resettlement and/or compensation of persons affected
by this project component (para. 4.27).
Rehabilitation/Reinforcement of the Distribution System of Hue
4.7        Hue (population 375,000), the political capital of Viet Nam from 1802 to 1945, is the
cultural, religious and educational center of the country. Its ancient monuments have been classified by
UNESCO as part of the world heritage and the Government attaches great significance to developing
Hue as a tourist center. Apart from its touristic importance, Hue has a number of industries and has a
good potential for industrial growth. The demand for electricity in 1993 was 17.5 MW, 74 Gwh p. a.,
with losses amounting to about 20% of which about 6% are estimated to be non-technical. A recent
detailed evaluation of Hue distribution concludes that: (a) the networks and their equipment are very old
and in a state of disrepair due to lack of spares; (b) the networks are under-sized and over-extended,
incurring excessive losses and voltage drops; and (c) the circuits are cluttered and clearances are below
standard, posing safety hazards. The distribution system is hardly adequate to meet existing demands
and is totally incapable of meeting future demand.
4.8        A detailed feasibility study for the rehabilitation and expansion of the Hue distribution
system was carried out by PC3 and reviewed and updated by consultants. A load forecast considering
detailed sector-wise analysis of demand growth and the current restrictions on electricity usage,
indicates the demand growing from 17.5 MW and 74 Gwh in 1993 to 42.8 MW and 170 Gwh in 2000,
reflecting an average growth rate of about 13%. The study presents the investments in the short and
medium term to rehabilitate and reinforce the network (including upgrading MV and LV voltages and
reconductoring), which would reduce its total losses from the current level of about 20% to about 10%
by 2000. In the absence of these investments the losses would increase to over 35%, if indeed the
network could withstand the increased stresses. The planning basis is considered to be reasonable and
practicable. The proposed project covers rehabilitation and expansion of the MV and LV lines and
MV/LV substations over the 1995-1997 period (see Annex 9, page 6 for details). Provision has been
made for resettlement and/or compensation of persons affected by this project component (para. 4.27).
Rehabilitation/Reinforcement of the Distribution System of Nhatrang
4.9        Nhatrang (population 280,000), the capital of Khanh Hoa Province, is one of the most
important tourist resorts in Viet Nam. It is also a cultural, economic and scientific center, with a
substantial industrial base. The demand for electricity in 1993 was 18 MW, 84 Gwh p. a., with losses
amounting to about 15% of which about 3.5% are estimated to be non-technical. A recent detailed
evaluation of Nhatrang distribution concludes that: (a) the networks and their equipment are very old
and in a state of disrepair due to lack of spares; (b) the networks are under-sized and over-extended,
incurring excessive losses and voltage drops; and (c) the circuits are cluttered and clearances below
standard, posing safety hazards. The distribution system is hardly adequate to meet existing demands
and is totally incapable of meeting future demand.
4.10       A detailed feasibility study for the rehabilitation and expansion of the Nhatrang distribution
system was carried out by PC3 and reviewed and updated by consultants. A load forecast considering
detailed sector-wise analysis of demand growth and the current restrictions on electricity usage,
indicates the demand growing from 18 MW and 83.8 Gwh in 1993 to 51.7 MW and 213 Gwh in 2000,
reflecting an average growth rate of about 16%. The study presents the investments in the short and
medium term to rehabilitate and reinforce the network (including upgrading MV and LV voltages and



-31-
reconductoring), which would reduce its total losses from the current level of about 15% to about 7.5%
by 2000. In the absence of these investments the losses would increase to over 28%, if indeed the
network could withstand the increased stresses. The planning basis is considered to be reasonable and
practicable. The proposed project covers rehabilitation and expansion of the MV and LV lines and
MV/LV substations over the 1995-1997 period (see Annex 9, page 8 for details). Provision has been
made for resettlement and/or compensation of persons affected by this project component (para. 4.27).
New Southern and Central Region Load Dispatch Centers
Strengthening of The National Load Dispatch Center
4.11       The northern, southern and central 220kV power systems currently operated by PC1, PC2
and PC3, respectively, are interconnected by a 500 kV transmission system. A National Load Dispatch
Center (NLDC), has been installed in the Ministry of Energy's (MOE) Hanoi headquarters and is being
operated by MOE staff. PC1 operates an existing Regional Load Dispatch Center (RLDC) from its
headquarters in Hanoi. The center was built about 10 years ago with assistance from the former USSR,
and provides basic monitoring functions for the northern region network. PC2 currently coordinates
load dispatch from its operations headquarters using basic telephone facilities and has comnnissioned a
new distribution system control center for Ho Chi Minh City. The latter is provided with supervisory
control and data acquisition facilities under a Swedish aid project. PC3 has rudimnentary supervision
facilities with limited PLC and VHF communications. Existing regional load dispatch facilities are
inadequate and need to be upgraded for proper monitoring and control of the respective regional power
systems and to facilitate optimal dispatch of power between regions.
4.12       A Conceptual Master Plan for the design and operation of the entire load dispatch system
in Viet Namn has been prepared by consultants. This plan lays down the philosophy of hierarchical
control of the system. The master plan also specifies the basic requirements of the hardware and
software for the SCADA and Energy Management (EMS) systems and the communication network.
Funding of the RLDCs for South and Central Viet Nam and components for extension of the National
Load Dispatch Center would be covered under the proposed project (Annex 9, pages 4, 10 and 18).
The RLDC for North is proposed to be funded by SIDA of Sweden. A building for housing the
southem RLDC has already been constructed whereas a new building would be built for the central
RLDC.
Southem and Central Region Training Centers
Equipment for The National Training Center
4.13       The existing facilities in the south, center and the north of Viet Nam for training of
technicians and staff of the respective power companies are ill-equipped and outdated primarily due to
lack of funding. While the building for the new training center in Hanoi, which would function as the
National Training Center, has been constructed, it is void of equipment and facilities. Several studies
have been made in the past for upgrading each of the training centers; an overall study reviewing the
training needs of the entire power sector and specifying a staged development of the training centers and
proposals for training was made by consultants. The proposed project covers the first phase of
upgrading the training facilities for the power sector and includes: (a) extensions of the existing works
facilities, provision of urgently needed training equipment, and training of trainers for the South and
Center; and (b) provision of equipment for the National Training Center (Annex 9, pages 5, 11 and
19).



-32-
Kronabuk-Nhatran2 220 kV Line and 220 kV Substations at Krongbuk and Nhatrang
4.14       The construction of the 500 kV North-Center-South transmission line and the establishment
of a 500/220 kV substation at Pleicu (see Grid Map), opens the way for providing reliable power to
central Viet Nam. The plan for transmitting power from Pleicu to Nhatrang via Krongbuk has been
approved by the Prime Minister and PC3 is already executing the Pleicu-Krongbuk section. PC3's
feasibility study and basic design for the 220 kV system expansion in central Viet Nam was reviewed
for IDA by consultants and found to be acceptable. The proposed project provides for the construction
of: (a) a 147 km, 336 AAAC conductor, single circuit 220 kV Krongbuk-Nhatrang transmission line;
(b) Krongbuk substation with one 220/110/20 kV, 63 MVA transformer, 3x220 kV and 2xll 0 kV
switching bays and 5x20 kV feeder outlets; and (c) Nhatrang substation with one 220/110/20 kV, 125
MVA transformer, 2x220 kV and 2xl 10 kV switching bays and 6x20 kV feeder outlets. Land for the
substations and right of way for the transmission line have already been secured. Provision has been
made for resettlement and/or compensation of persons affected by this project component (para. 4.28).
Reinforcement of The 110 kV substations at Nhatrang. Cau Do and Lien Tri.
4.15       Based on detailed demand projections by PC3, reinforcement of 110 kV substations is
necessary to meet the demand growth in the areas of Nhatrang, Cau Do and Lientri in the north of
central Viet Nam (see Grid Map). The project provides for the installation of: (a) lx25 MVA, 110/20
kV transformer, 4xll O kV and 4x20 kV feeders at Nhatrang substation; (b) lx25 MVA, 110/35 kV
transformer, 2x110 kV and 6x35 kV feeders at Cao Do substation; and (d) lx25 MVA, 110/35 kV
transformer, 2x1 10 kV and 6x35 kV feeders at Lien Tri substation.
Consulting Studies for Proiect Mananement and Technical Assistance Engineering Studies for Future
Hydro Proiects
4.16       Based on a detailed evaluation of the needs of the various implementing agencies,
provision has been made in the project for adequate staff-months (SM) of expatriate consulting services
to assist in engineering, design, procurement and construction supervision for: (a) the Ba Ria combined
cycle conversion (100 SM); (b) HCMC distribution (60 SM); (c) Southern RLDC (60 SM); (d)
Southern Training Centre, including training (50 SM); (e) Hue/Nhatrang distribution (50 SM); (f)
Central RLDC (60 SM); (g) Central Training Center, including training (50 SM); (h) 220 kV line and
substations (30 SM); (i) National LDC (30 SM); and (j) engineering studies for Dai Ninh and Son La
Hydropower projects (60 SM each). The terms of reference for all the project related consulting
assistance have been agreed with the implementing agencies.
Technical Assistance for Demand Side Management.
4.17       While there is a growing awareness of the need for Demand Side Management (DSM) in
Government and utility circles, there has been very limited application of energy efficiency measures
and other DSM activities in Viet Nam. There is also very little energy end-use data available in the
country. Viet Nam needs to implement all available cost effective DSM measures to use electricity in
the most efficient manner, commensurate with the country's development. The main objectives of the
study (Terms of Reference are at Annex 10) are to: (a) identify a menu of DSM opportunities in the
industrial, commercial and residential sectors; (b) prioritize and evaluate these DSM sector alternatives,
based on their energy sector impact and cost effectiveness; (c) define an appropriate institutional and
regulatory framework for DSM program implementation; (d) introduce a resource planning approach



-33-
(e.g Integrated Resource Planning (IRP)) which would permit the cost-effective assessment of all
sU.   and demand energy resource options; and finally (e) identify DSM components that could be
coL   red for financing under an IDA Energy Sector Credit. Agreement was reached at negotiations
that wle Borrower would furnish to IDA for review and comments: (a) the findings of the study; and (b)
its proposals for the implementation of the study's recommendations, and thereafter implement the
proposals taking into consideration IDA's commnents.
Technical Assistance for Power Sector Reforrn & Institutional Strengthening.
4.18     To meet Government's overall objectives of reforming state enterprises and moving from
centrally planned to market-oriented mechanisms, two major technical assistance initiatives are planned.
The first, being conducted by the Banks ESMAP is focussed on an immediate need articulated by the
Government. This technical assistance is designed to assist the Government and EVN in making the
transition from the existing power sector structure to the new structure.  This effort is based on the
principles of: (a) improving the operational efficiency of the sector; (b) commercialization and
corporatization of the constituent operations to provide greater managerial and financial autonomy; (c)
developing an appropriate legal and regulatory framework that would allow for greater enterprise
autonomy and requisite government regulatory oversight; and (d) a financially viable and open sector
structure that allows for increased private involvement in financing sector expansion. (Terms of
Reference in Annex 8).
4.19     The second, technical assistance program under the proposed project, directed at much
needed institutional strengthening, is being financed by the Japanese Grant Facility. This technical
assistance would focus on the development of appropriate organizational structures, adoption of
commercial management practices, budget and control systems, reporting procedures and information
flows, under the reformed sector structure. (Terms of Reference in Annex 11). The study will
reconmmend: (a) appropriate levels of consolidation of accounting statements and balance sheets of the
subordinate entities under EVN; (b) organization of line and staff functions of the newly defined
entities; and (c) the operational, financial and MIS reporting requirements within the new entities.  A
complementary technical assistance program is being funded by ADB which focuses on the development
of cost and financial accounting systems (Terms of Reference in Annex 6). Close coordination of these
complementary technical assistance programs would be ensured from the outset. Agreement was
reached at negotiations that the Borrower would furnish to IDA for review and comments: (a) the
findings of the studies; and (b) its proposals for the implementation of the studies' recommendations,
and thereafter implement the proposals taking into account IDA's comments.
B. Implementation
4.20           PC2 and PC3 would be responsible for implementing the major portion of the project,
managing components falling within their jurisdiction in South and Central Viet Nam, respectively.
The technical experts of the MOE would be responsible for implementing the strengthening of the
National Load Dispatch Center, while PCI will assist MOE in implementing the component for
strengthening of the National Training Center in Hanoi. The Personnel Department of MOE will
manage the technical assistance studies relating to Power Sector Institutional Strengthening and Power
Sector Reform and Restructuring, while the Energy Institute will manage the technical assistance study



-34-
for Demand Side Management. Both PC2 and PC3 have substantial in-house expertise in engineering
and design; this would be reinforced through assistance from PIDC2 and PIDC1, respectively.
Adequate consulting assistance is being provided under the project (para. 4.16) to assist the
implementing agencies in developing designs and bid documents, evaluating bids and preparing
evaluation reports, project management including construction supervision and progress reporting.
Draft bidding documents following the Bank guidelines have already been prepared by consultants for
HCMC, Hue and Nhatrang distribution systems, the Southern and Central RLDCs and the 220 kV
system components. These will be refined and finalized with the assistance of the consultants employed
under the project.
4.21           Both PC2 and PC3 have prepared Project Implementation Plans following the Bank
guidelines; these indicate the organizational arrangements for project management and the
implementation bar charts.  Project Management Units (with a Project Manager and staff positions)
will be set up within PC2 and PC3 specifically for managing the IDA-assisted project components (see
Charts 4 and 5). Bidding Evaluation Commnittees (having representation from the MOE) will be set up
for PC2 and PC3 for approving bid documents and contract awards.
4.22           The Power Distribution Company in HCMC and the provincial distribution authorities
in Hue and Nhatrang will play a major role in managing the distribution projects and constructing the
networks. About 50% of installation work would be let out on contract to local firms through
competitive bidding and the rest done through forced account. Construction for the 220 kV lines and
the 220kV and 110 kV substations will be handled by PC3 in a similar manner. While PC2's load
dispatch department has adequate expertise in managing the RLDC project, PC3 will avail itself of
substantial assistance from PIDC1 and MOE. Both PC2 and PC3 have adequate experience in handling
the training center components, with necessary expatriate consultancy assistance. The Ba Ria combined
cycle component will be managed by PC2 with the assistance of PIDC2; its installation will be let out
on turnkey basis.
4.23           The bar charts for implementing the project components and the key project dates are
given in Annex 12. The major portion of the project implementation would be over the 1995-1997
period. The Vietnamese institutions are technically well experienced in implementing the project
components and with the expatriate consulting assistance provided under the project, no substantive
problems are foreseen in efficient and timely implementation of the project.  The implementing
arrangements are satisfactory to IDA.
Monitoring and Reporting
4.24           Satisfactory procedures for monitoring the progress of the project in terms of physical
execution and financial reports were agreed, at negotiations, with each implementing agency. It would
also be agreed that each agency will furnish quarterly progress reports. An Implementation Completion
Report (ICR) will be drafted by IDA not later than six months after completion of the Credit and
agreement was reached with MOE, PC2 and PC3 to assist in its preparation. The agencies will adopt
the plan for the operational phase of the project and together with IDA, define the performance
indicators to be used to monitor operations and development impact. The Agencies will also prepare
and make available to IDA their own evaluation reports, including summary reports which will be
attached unedited to the ICR. The evaluation would assess the project execution and initial operation,
its costs and benefits, IDA's performance, its own performance of the obligations under the Credit
Agreement, and the extent to which the purposes of the Credit were achieved.



-35-
Supervision Plan
4.25           Supervision of this project will extend over a period of five years, 1995-1999. The
key issues that would be focused upon are: (a) review of Viet Nam's power development plan in
keeping with changes in the economic scenario; (b) a continuing dialogue with the Government on
tariffs for the power sector; (c) monitoring of compliance with financial covenants to assure the
financial health of the PCs while undertaking large investment programs; (d) monitoring of the
implementation of the environmental impact mitigation measures for Ba Ria and rehabilitation plans for:
(i) the 220 kV transmission line and substations; and (ii) people likely to be displaced due to
construction of the distribution lines and substations; and (e) technical supervision of physical
implementation of the project components. The IDA missions would also assist the Government in
analyzing issues and options in power sector institutional strengthening and in formulating strategy and
concrete plans for DSM. Supervision of the project would require expertise in power engineering,
economics, financial analysis and rehabilitation. Three missions annually for a period of three years
(normally coinciding with preparatory missions for future IDA-assisted projects) are foreseen for
adequate supervision of this project. The total estimated staff inputs are: (a) power engineer, economist
and financial analyst -- 24 staff-weeks; and (b) rehabilitation specialist -- 9 staff-weeks. Key project
performance indicators that would be used for supervision are given in Annex 13. These performance
indicators cover: (a) the reduction of losses; (b) the reduction of accounts receivable; and (c) the timely
completion of Load Dispatch and Training Centers - all of which are linked to improving the efficiency
of the power sector operations, which is a primary objective of the project. Also, setting of target dates
for the completion of institutional studies would contribute towards timely sequencing of reforms in the
sector. Finally, monitoring of target completion dates for major components of the project would
strengthen project implementation discipline, while environmental and resettlement related monitoring
would ensure environmentally and socially acceptable development.
C. Environment and Resettlement
4.26           All load dispatch and training centers and the expansions of the 110 kV substations of
Nhatrang, Cau Do and Lien Tri are on existing land plots and in some cases in existing buildings and
do not pose any environmental issues. Rehabilitation of old, cluttered distribution networks in HCMC,
Hue and Nhatrang, predominantly using insulated conductors, largely running along existing corridors,
would contribute to greater safety and present better aesthetic appearance. No PCB is used in the
power transformers that would be replaced under the project. The routes of distribution lines and
locations of distribution substations may in exceptional cases involve displacement of some people. The
220 kV Krongbuk-Nhatrang transmission line route traversing through agricultural and tree-crop land,
does not encroach on ecologically sensitive areas. However, 80 houses would need to be relocated
along the line route. Although the line traverses through areas inhabited by ethnic people, care has
been taken in routing to ensure that no ethnic people are affected by the project. The 220 kV Krongbuk
and Nhatrang substations are located on grass land.
Distribution Systems for Ho Chi Minh City. Hue and Nhatran,
4.27           The detailed design of the MV and LV distribution systems for HCMC, Hue and
Nhatrang would be finalized later. A detailed Resettlement Action Plan (RAP) for this component



-36-
cannot, therefore, be prepared at this stage. The RAP is being prepared in two phases: (a) RAP Phase-
1 (see Annex 14 for details), which has already been prepared, includes: (i) the resettlement principles;
(ii) institutional and legal framework including entitlement policies; (iii) implementation arrangements;
(iv) peoples' participation in implementation; (v) grievance redressal mechanisms; and (vi) provision for
internal and extemal monitoring; and (b) RAPs Phase-2, which will consist of: (i) results of the socio-
economic census and socio-economic survey of the project affected persons (PAPs) and properties to be
affected; (ii) detailed compensation and/or resettlement and rehabilitation entitlements of various
categories of PAPs; (iii) a timetable for implementation; (iv) institutional responsibilities for
implementation; (v) a detailed budget for funding the various compensation and rehabilitation measures;
and (vi) intemal and extemal monitoring arrangements. The census and socio-economic surveys under
the RAPs, Phase-2 will be completed as soon as possible but at least 6 months prior to the estimated
date for commencement of construction. It was agreed at negotiations that the RAPs, Phase-2 will be:
(a) furnished to IDA no later than 3 months prior to their implementation; (b) undertaken only after
approval by IDA and the Government; and (c) completed at least 1 month before the beginning of
construction work in any given area. The Phase-I RAP was agreed with the Govermnent prior to
negotiations. Approval of the Phase-2 RAPs by IDA and the Govermnent would be a condition for
credit disbursement against expenditures incurred against the distribution systems sub-components of the
project.
220 kV Kron2buk-Nhatran2 Line and Substations at Kron2buk and Nhatrang
4.28           For the 220 kV Krongbuk-Nhatrang line and terminal substations at Krongbuk and
Nhatrang, a RAP has been prepared for the 85 families that would be affected by the transmission line
(see Annex 14 for details). Only land directly under the transmission towers and the houses in the right
of way (ROW) will need to be acquired. Land, not directly under the towers, can continue to be used
for agricultural purposes with some restrictions on the height of trees. The PAPs will be relocated
close to their present location in order to ensure that their socio-economic lifestyles will not be affected.
The form of compensation for land will be "land for land". Compensation will be paid at replacement
cost for houses and structures and at market rates for trees and crops. The RAP will be implemented
by PC3 with the involvement of PAPs and the peoples' committees at the provincial, district and
commune levels. Adequate mechanisms have been provided for the redressal of grievances and for
external and internal supervision and monitoring. The RAP is in compliance with the Bank's
operational directives and is acceptable to IDA. The RAP was agreed with the Government prior to
negotiations. It was agreed at negotiations that PC3 would carry out the RAP as approved by IDA and
the Government.
Ba Ria Combined Cycle Conversion
4.29           A detailed environmental assessment (Annex 22, Ref 9a and 9b; Annex 15 - EA
Overview) has concluded that with proper design and mitigation measures, atmospheric impacts (NO,
and noise levels) and aquatic impacts (cooling water temperature, chlorine concentration and impact on
shrimp farming and mangroves) would be within acceptable limits. The EA has been approved by the
Government. An alternative cooling system using cooling towers is being studied. If this option is
decided upon, there would be no need for creating a cooling water lagoon in the river estuary and the



-37-
corresponding impact on the marine environment would disappear.- In the event a cooling water
lagoon is required, a part of a cooperative shrimp farm will need to be acquired. The farm has more
land than can effectively be utilized by the present number of members. Hence, acquisition of a part of
this shrimp farm will not adversely affect the livelihood of any of its members. Compensation rates
acceptable to the cooperative have been agreed upon between the farmers, the local district peoples'
committee and PC2. It was agreed during negotiations that PC2 would: (a) design the plant and follow
appropriate mitigation measures; (b) set up an environmental unit and an environmental coordinator as
part of the management structure of the power station, as outlined in the EA document; and (c)
compensate the shrimp farming community at rates that have been mutually agreed upon.
D. Cost Estimates
4.30            The total cost of the project (including capitalized interest during construction) is
estimated at US$247.9 million, with a foreign exchange component of US$165.9 million. Physical
contingencies are assumed at 10% of the base cost for all project components. Price contingencies are
estimated on the basis of escalation factors of 5% per annum for local cost components and 2.3% per
annum for foreign cost components, following the Bank's latest forecasts. Table 4.1 summarizes the
cost estimates for the project (details are at Annex 9).
E. Financing Plan
4.31            The financing plan for the project is shown in Table 4.2. The proposed IDA credit of
US$165 million equivalent would meet almost 100% of the foreign cost of the project and about 67% of
project financing requirements. The proposed IDA credit would be made to the Government at IDA's
standard rate for a 40 year terrn including 5 years of grace on repayment of principal. Of the total
Credit amount of US$165 million equivalent, US$117 million equivalent would be onlent to PC2 and
US$40 million equivalent to PC3. An amount of US$8 million would be used by the Government for
project components to be executed by the MOE. The credit would be on-lent to PC2 and PC3 in US
dollars at a fixed interest rate of 6.9% per annum, with repayment over 20 years, including a grace
period of 5 years, and foreign exchange risk being borne by PC2 and PC3. The finalization of
subsidiary loan agreements between the Government and PC2 and PC3, acceptable to IDA, would be a
condition of effectiveness of the IDA credit.

F. Procurement
4.32            About 93%  (US$153.5 million equivalent) of the IDA credit would be used for
financing goods procured through International Competitive Bidding (ICB) using the Bank guidelines.
In the evaluation of bids obtained following ICB procedures, a margin of preference equal to 15 % of
the CIF bid price of imported goods or the actual customs duties and import taxes, whichever is less,
will be allowed for domestic manufactures. About 6% (US$10 million equivalent) of the credit amount
would be used for financing consulting services procured following the Bank procedures for the
employment of consultants. About 1% (US$1.6 million equivalent) of the credit would be used for
financing specialized equipment (including testing and measuring equipment) using the following
procedures complying with the Bank guidelines: (a) Limited International Bidding (LIB), aggregating
US$1.2 million equivalent; and (b) International Shopping (IS) aggregating US$0.4 million equivalent.
Contracts under these procedures would not exceed the equivalent of US$200,000 each for LIB and
US$50,000 each for IS.
4.33            The bid documents would follow the text of the Bank's Standard Bidding Documents.
All bid documents, contract award recommendations and contracts for goods and services would be
subject to prior review and approval by IDA. The total number of procurement packages is foreseen to
be: (a) ICB - 20 packages (Annex 16), 13 for PC3, 5 for PC2 and 2 for MOE; and (b) LIB and IS -
about 14 packages. A total of about 620 staff-months of consulting services will be engaged under 11
contracts (para 4.16).
4.34            Local contracts for installation would not be financed from the IDA credit. About
50% of installation work for distribution system rehabilitation and expansion, transmission line and
substations would be contracted to local firms through a competitive bidding process satisfactory to
IDA. The balance of such installation work would be undertaken on force-account basis using the PCs
own resources including those of their subsidiaries. These personnel have long experience in executing



-40-
installation work of this nature. Implementation of the Ba Ria combined cycle plant component would
be on turnkey basis.
4.35           Table 4.3 summarizes the procurement arrangements for the components expected to
be financed out of the proposed IDA credit.
G. Disbursements
4.36           The IDA credit would be disbursed against: (a) 100% of foreign expenditures, or
100% of local expenditures (ex-factory cost) for goods procured through ICB; (b) 50% of local
expenditures for other items procured locally; (c) 100% of foreign expenditures for goods purchased
through LIB or IS; and (d) 100% of expenditures for consulting services, excluding taxes. As no
contract is expected to be less than about US$200,000 equivalent (except for a few contracts under IS
procedures), Statement of Expenditures (SOE) procedures would not be followed.  To facilitate
disbursements, three Special Accounts would be established in US currency for PC2, PC3 and MOE on
terms and conditions satisfactory to IDA with deposits of US$4.0 million (PC2), US$1.5 million (PC3)
and US$0.6 million (MOE). Replenishment applications should be submitted monthly or when the
account is drawn by 30% of the authorized allocation, whichever occurs first. For withdrawal outside
of the Special Accounts (applications for direct payment or for issuance of Special Commitments) a
minimum application value of 20% of the authorized allocation of the Special Accounts would be
observed.
4.37           Retroactive financing would be permitted to the extent bf US$5.0 million equivalent
for payments made, prior to the date of the Credit Agreement but after August 23, 1994 (the appraisal
starting date), for contracting urgently required goods and consulting services. This is necessary to
meet the project implementation schedule.
4.38           Annex 17 gives the disbursement schedule for the proposed IDA credit and the
standard profile of disbursements for power projects in Asia. The credit is assumed to be disbursed
about three years faster than the profile, based on actual performance of the Vietnamese on other power
projects and the preparatory work already undertaken. The project is expected to be completed by June
30, 1998 and the closing date for the credit would be June 30, 1999.

Chapter V
Financial Aspects
A. Introduction
5.1        The accounting procedures of PC2 and PC3 comprise several features which make a
conventional financial analysis difficult (para. 3.18). Hence, the income statements and balance sheets
for FY92 and FY93 were modified to conform, to the extent possible, to the concept of accrued income
and expenses: (a) revenues from sales of power were recomputed to an accrual basis; (b) foreign
exchange equivalents were restated to those in effect at the end of the respective financial year; (c)
depreciation on fully depreciated assets was eliminated; and (d) receivables were corrected in line with
the revenue adjustment. In addition, modifications were made to the income statements, particularly in
regard to certain operational expense items (para. 3.18) which PC2 and PC3 used to simply capitalize
on the balance sheet. Furthermore, revenues of D 140 billion were added to the 1993 income statement
of PC2 to offset depreciation expenses disallowed by the Government.
5.2        Thus modified, the accounts of PC2 and PC3 serve as a reasonable basis for the financial
projections. Until such time that the studies (para. 3.19) are completed and accounts changed to
comply with international utility practices, the indices discussed in this chapter need to be viewed with
caution.
B. Past and Present Financial Performance
5.3        The Government's policy reforms in the power sector meant to give all PCs increased
autonomy in the operation and management of their assets. To this end, Decree No. 388 (Formation
and Dissolution of SOEs) was enacted in 1976. This allowed the PCs to engage in business activities
with a degree of independence which up to that time was not possible. However, defined corporate
objectives, mechanisms to foster managerial efficiency or financial discipline, and the institutional and
organizational systems and skills necessary to translate this increased autonomy into actual practice are
still not available. Thus, while sector reforms allowed the PCs to be responsible for their day-to-day
operations, matters relating to planning, budgeting, staffing, appointing of high level staff, contracting,
pricing, and financing of investments are still subject to Government approval, through the MOE.
While the resolution creating the PCs gives them the responsibility to manage and utilize their resources
"paying attention to high rates of return", and to continuously accumulate funds for the Govermnent and
themselves, there is no explicit financial mandate to ensure that the PCs' revenues be sufficient to meet
operating expenses, depreciation and interest charges.
5.4        A summary of the actual operating results of PC2 and PC3 for FY92 and FY93 is
presented in Table 5.1; the detailed statements are given in Annexes 18 and 19.
