Annex 11
Page 1 of 4
VIET NAM
Power Sector Rehabilitation and Expansion Project
Power Sector: Institutional Strengthening
Terms of Reference for Consulting Study
A. Background
1.         The Vietnamese power sector is currently  undergoing  a significant structural
transformation. This structural change would involve the creation of an umbrella power enterprise (i.e.
Electricity of Vietnam, EVN) that would supervise the operations of subordinate entities engaged in the
core activities of generation, transmission and distribution.
2.         This technical assistance (TA) project has been designed to assist the restructured entities
in meeting the operational and management challenges of this complex structural change.  The
realization of efficiency gains at the enterprise level is a key objective of the exercise. The consulting
services to be financed under this technical assistance component would develop a masterplan for
implementing internal changes in organization, and the corresponding accounting, budgeting, and
financial management systems, within the restructured power system in Viet Nnam. These changes will
reflect the principles of increasing management autonomy and accountability, and improving the flow of
cost and financial information to assist management in its operational and financial decisions.
3.         Two complementary initiatives are planned to assist the Ministry of Energy (MOE) in
restructuring the power sector, and improving the accounting systems and practices of the constituent
power entities. The first, which is currently underway, is the Power Sector Reform and Restructuring
Study. This effort is intended to assist MOE/EVN in developing a framework and sequence for
reforming the power sector. The second program of technical assistance, under ADB funding, is
intended to improve the financial and accounting systems in the power sector. To achieve the full
benefits of organizational reform and improved financial reporting and monitoring systems, it is crucial
that this technical assistance component be closely integrated with the above activities from the outset.
B. Scope of Work
4.         The overall scope of work is to develop practical and clearly defined recommendations for
organizational reforms, and the introduction of modem financial management practices and systems in
the subordinate power entities under EVN. In addressing this issue, the underlying principle is to
improve the operational efficiency and financial viability of the various business units and entities
related to EVN.
5.         In view of the need to develop a coherent approach to the intended organizational reform
and introduction of new financial and accounting management systems, the work is divided into two
phases:



-108-
Annex II
Page 2 of 4
Phase 1:
6.         Development of workplan to meet the objective of Phase 2 (below) based on the outputs of
the May 1995 sector restructuring workshop, and more importantly on the final approval of the draft
charter for EVN by the Government of Viet Nam which will lay out the boundaries of the different
operational entities under EVN. This workplan will:
(a)   establish the key client working groups who will work closely with the consultants on a
day-to-day basis. The designated Vietnamese staff will be identified by the relevant
institutions and will work with the Consultant for the duration of the technical assistance
component.
(b)   outline the information requirements, and program of field visits.
(c)   develop in consultation with the ADB-funded consultant team a viable program  for
collaboration to avoid any unnecessary overlap and repetition of tasks.
Phase 2:
7.         Preparation of a Masterplan recommending appropriate organizational and management
structures of the subordinate entities under EVN. The main focus of this Masterplan would be to
recommend: (a) appropriate levels and procedures for consolidating accounting statements and balance
sheets of the subordinate power entities under EVN; (b) the organization of line and staff functions of
the newly defined entities; and (c) the operational, financial and MIS reporting requirements within and
between the new entities.
8.         As the ADB-funded technical assistance will be closely related to this phase of work, close
collaboration will be maintained at all times with the ADB funded consultant team.
The detailed scope of this masterplan is as follows:
(a)  redefinition of the functional boundaries of the different departments, work units and
subsidiaries within each independent and dependent accounting entity under EVN. This
could include the merging, separation or elimination of certain functions.
Correspondingly, this could involve the strengthening or expansion of certain functions,
e.g. financial operations at the level of EVN and the main generation and transmission
companies.
(b)   redefinition of job functions/descriptions as appropriate to fit the recommended
reorganization. The conunuication and reporting channels should also be defined.
Close working group sessions with managers and staff will be required to make sure that
the developments are totally in conformity with their needs.
(c)   redefinition of accounting units and activities, reporting requirements, formats for
information flow and frequency of such information exchange. This task will develop a
basic design for the new financial and accounting information system. It is of crucial



-109-
Annex 11
Page 3 of 4
importance that this basic design of the financial and accounting management information
system be totally consistent with the proposed reorganization of business processes and
procedures.
(d)   development of a financial planning system, including the introduction of operational
objectives and planned allocation of resources in the form of operating expense budgets
and capital expenditure budgets, and the frequency of issuance.
(e)  redefinition of the process of setting performance targets, and the systems for controlling
and monitoring them in practice. This would include policies and procedures, related
analytical techniques, and mechanical tools to ensure project planning, formulation,
justification, management and control of budgets, including analysis of budget variances.
It is once again of crucial importance that this be completely integrated with the
management/financial information system that is to developed.
(f)  improving the planning and control of operational support functions or central service
functions, such as, maintenance and work planning/preparation, materials management,
procurement, quality control, transportation, personnel management, etc.
(g)   preparation of a detailed scope of tasks and a clearly defined implementation strategy for
the adoption of the above recommendations. The implementation strategy will be divided
into monitorable actions and targets with a timetable. Identification and definition of
training needs and specific programs for imparting this training to the staff and
management of the different power sector entities.
9.         The TA's scope would cover the following main heads:  (a) Strategic Planning and
Organizational Structure; (b) Management Information and Budgeting Systems (MIS); Computerizing
and Data Processing; (c) Cost and Financial Accounting Systems (this aspect is being covered by an
ADB funded study and only coordination is required under this TA); (d) Human Resource
Development; (e) Materials Management; (f) Financial Management; and (g) Customer Relations.
Plan of Work
10.        Execution of the TA will be based on collaboration and consultation between the
Consultant(s) and designated staff of the power companies and MOE concerned with organizational and
management matters. To this end, the bulk of the institutional strengthening tasks should be carried out
in Viet Nam. The designated Vietnamese staff will be identified by the relevant institutions prior to the
start-up of this component and will work with the Consultant(s) for the duration of the component.
11.        The Consultant(s) will prepare two Reports: a preliminary report of their findings and
recommendations which would be discussed with the Vietnamese authorities and IDA. A draft Final
Report would be submitted, taking into account the outputs of the complimentary TAs and would be
finalized, taking into account the views of the Vietnamese authorities and IDA.



-110-
Annex 1 1
Page 4 of 4
Tasks
12.        The following main tasks are visualized: (a) review  the existing organization and
mianagement structures of the power companies, including the structure of all major functional units,
taking into account their tasks and inter-organizational relationships; (b) identify weaknesses, if any, in
the existing organizational structure and recommend changes keeping in mind the: (i) purposes and
objectives of the organization; (ii) functional areas to be covered; (iii) specialization and division of
work; (iv) line and staff functions and (v) the need to formalize reporting relationships and lines of
authority; (c) assess the staffing pattern and recruitment needs to determine and classify the various
positions required and prepare a staffing proposal based on the recommnended organizational structures
and interrelationships; (d) prepare job specifications and job manuals setting out suitable qualifications
and experience for various categories of employees; (e) review and analyze technical practices and
operating procedures and recommend systems aimed at making those technical practices more uniform;
(f) review and analyze current financial management practices, recommend changes as required and
identify training needs to upgrade existing skills; and (g) analyze the information system in place and
recommend adjustments thereto, or alternatively introduce a management information system
appropriate to the power company's size and stage of development which will include inter-alia: (i)
information to be collected, where when and by whom; (ii) design of various reporting fornats for
different functional departments including construction, generation, transmission distribution,
commercial, personnel, statistical and administrative; (iii) flow of reports; (iv) procedures for synthesis
and analysis of reports; (v) procedures for follow-up action and; (vi) comprehensive review of the
organization, practices and procedures used by the power company's commercial and administrative
departments; (h) review and recommend improvements to the power companies' (i) administrative
procedures; and (ii) internal control systems, rules and regulations to cover establishment of procedures,
adequacy and direction of communication flow and gaps therein, inter-department relationships and
duplication of actions; and (i) maintain at all times a liaison with the ADB-funded study on cost and
financial accounting systems.
13.        The Government would provide accommodation and office facilities to expatriate advisors,
interpretation/translation services and local travel.

Section 1
Introduction
A. The Project
1.         The Power Sector Rehabilitation and Expansion Project (the Project) includes inter-alia
rehabilitation and expansion of medium voltage (MV) and low voltage (LV) electricity distribution
networks, comprising construction of MV and LV lines (overhead and underground) and MV/LV
substations in Ho Chi Minh City (Part A. 1 of the Project) and in Hue and Nhatrang (Part B. 1 of the
Project) to be undertaken by the PC2 and PC3, respectively. A separate Resettlement Action Plan for
the 220kv Krongbuk-Nhatrang power transmission line and 220kv terminal substations at Krongbuck
and Nhatrang (Part B. 1 of the Project) has been prepared by PC3 and approved by the Government of
the Socialist Republic of Viet Nam, dated March 27, 1995.
B. Distribution System Resettlement Action Plan Phase 1 (RAP-1)
2.         Every effort will be made to expand the distribution network under Parts A. 1 and B. 1 of
the Project by utilizing the land already available with PC2 and PC3 (along existing routes). In
exceptional circumstances acquisition of additional land and/or houses and the resettlement of people
losing the totality of their land and/or houses or a significant part thereof would be unavoidable.
However, the final routing of lines and location of new substations, which may require acquisition of
land and/or houses would be finalized during the detailed design stage under Project implementation.
To adequately address compensation, resettlement and rehabilitation of the people to be affected by
these Parts of the Project (PAPs), the Resettlement Action Plan (RAP) has been divided into Phase 1
RAP (RAP-1) and Phase 2 RAP (RAP-2). This is the Phase-i RAP.
3.         The principle objective of the RAP is to ensure that all PAPs will be compensated and
rehabilitated to assist them to improve, or at least maintain, their living conditions and income earning
capacity at the pre-Project levels.
4.         This RAP-I has been prepared by the PC2 and PC3 and approved by the Government of
the Socialist Republic of Viet Nam on March 27, 1995. It lays down the principles and objectives,
legal and institutional framework, modes of compensation and rehabilitation, peoples participation
features and grievances procedures that will guide the resettlement and rehabilitation of the (PAPs).
Each of PC2 and PC3 will prepare a RAP-2 for Parts A. 1 and B. 1 of the Project, respectively. Each
RAP-2 will include: (a) results of the census and socio-economic survey of the PAPs and properties to
be affected; (b) detailed compensation and/or resettlement and rehabilitation entitlements of various
categories of PAPs; (c) a timetable for implementation of the RAP-2; (d) allocation of the institutional
responsibilities for implementation; (e) a detailed budget for funding the various compensation and
rehabilitation measures; and (f) internal and external monitoring arrangements.
5.         The census and socio-economic surveys under each of the RAP-2 would be completed as
soon as possible but no later than six months prior to the estimated date for commencement of the
works under the respective Part of the Project. Each of the RAP-2 will be furnished to the International



-127-
Annex 14
Page 4 of 22
Development Association (IDA) for consideration as soon as possible but no later than three months
prior to the actual initiation of the works under the respective Part of the Project. Compensation and
resettlement and rehabilitation activities under Parts A. 1 and B. I of the Project will only commence
after IDA has found acceptable the respective RAP-2 and the Government of the Socialist Republic of
Viet Nam has approved it. These activities will be completed at least one month before the beginning
of works in each site under said Parts of the Project.
C. Project Affected People (PAPS)
6.         The PAPs include the following persons to be identified in the census and socio-economic
surveys under each of the RAP-2:
(a)   persons whose houses are in part or in toto affected by the Project;
(b)   persons whose premise and/or agricultural land is in part or in toto affected (permanently
or temporarily) by the Project; and
(c)   persons whose businesses are affected in part or in toto (temporarily or permanently) by
the Project.
D. Resetthment Principles and Objectives
7.         The principles outlined in the World Bank's Operational Directives 4.30 have been
adopted in preparing the RAP. In this regard the following principles and objectives would be applied:
(a)   Resettlement will be minimized as much as possible.
(b)   All PAPs residing or cultivating land in the Project area as of the date of the socio-
economic survey are entitled to compensation for their losses and/or income rehabilitation.
Lack of land use right certificate will not bar the PAP from compensation and/or income
restoration.
(c)   PAPs will be compensated, resettled and rehabilitated so as to improve their standard of
living or at least maintain their current standards at pre-Project level after resettlement.
(d)   The means of resettlement and rehabilitation are: compensation at replacement cost for
houses and other structures, agricultural land for land of equal productive capacity
acceptable to the PAP, replacement of premise land at least of equal size acceptable to the
PAP, and transfer allowances.
(e)   Replacement premise and agricultural land will be as close as possible to the land that was
lost, acceptable to the PAP.
(f)   The resettlement transition period will be minimized and land for land and/or cash
compensation should be provided to the PAPs no later than one month prior to the
expected start-up date of works in the respective Project site.



-128-
Annex 14
Page 5 of 22
(g)  Resettlement and land acquisition plans will be carried out following consultation with the
PAPs.
(h)  The previous level of community services and resources will be maintained or improved
after resettlement.
(i)   Financial and physical resources for resettlement and rehabilitation will be made available
as and when required.
(j)  Institutional arrangements will ensure effective and timely design, planning and
implementation of the RAP.
(k) Internal and external effective and timely monitoring will be provided on the
implementation of the RAP.
Section 2
Institutional and Legal Framework
A. Institutional Framework
8.         The responsibility for implementing the RAP are as follows:
(a)   The respective Power Company (PC) has overall responsibility for planning and
implementing the RAP within its jurisdiction. For this purpose, the respective PC, will
coordinate with the respective District Peoples' Committees (DPCs).  The peoples
committees at the commune level will discuss the various aspects of the RAP with the
PAPs.
(b)   Funds for the resettlement program will be provided by PC2/PC3 based on decisions,
reached through negotiations between local governments (district and commune peoples
committees) and the PAPs.
(c)   Provincial, District, and Commune People's Committees will organize and carry out the
RAP within the areas of their responsibility under the supervision of the respective PC.
B. Legal Framework
9.         The overall objective of the RAP is guided by Article 27 of the Land Law of 1993 (as
amplified by Government decree No 90-CP of 17th August 1994) enacted by the National Assembly of
the Socialist Republic of Viet Nam on July 1993.  Article 27 provides that: 'In case of utmost
necessity, when the State recovers land being used by a land user, for national defense, security,
national benefit, or public benefit purposes, the land user shall be given compensation for the
damages".



-129-
Annex 14
Page 6 of 22
10.        Compensation for land and fixed assets (e.g. houses) is defined by the Government Decree
No. 87-CP of the 17th of August 1994, which provides for land for land compensation and cash for
land, when land is not available, at rates established by Government. These rates have been established
for purposes of leasing government land, acquisition of land by government for national purposes, and
for tax value for issuing land use rights certificates.
Section 3
Entitlement Policy
11.        PAP will be entitled to the following types of compensation as they apply to individual
situations according to the eligibility and entitlement categories defined above.
12.        PAPs losing agricultural land will be compensated as follows:
(a)  the general mechanism for compensation of lost agricultural land will be through "land for
land" arrangements of equal productive capacity, satisfactory to the PAP. However, if
such land is not available in the vicinity, compensation in cash; at full replacement cost,
can be provided as mutually agreed between the PAP and the relevant peoples' committee.
If the portion of the land to be lost represents 20% or less of the total area of the land,
cash compensation, at full replacement cost, will be provided to the PAP; and
(b)   PAPs who are forced to relocate or lose agricultural land shall be compensated with the
market price for the loss of standing crops. In case of loss of fruit or industrial trees,
these will be compensated at market price.
13.        PAPs whose houses will be affected by the Project will be provided with:
(a)   replacement residential (premises) land of equivalent size; and (ii) cash compensation,
reflecting full replacement cost of the structure without depreciation.
(b)  if the premise land and/or structure is only partially being affected by the Project and the
remaining part of the structure is habitable, either the entire premise land and structure
would be acquired from the PAP and compensation paid as under sub-paragraph (a), or
alternatively, compensation in cash reflecting full replacement cost of the portion of the
premise land and/or structure affected will be provided as mutually agreed between the
PAP and the relevant peoples' committee; and
(c)  tenants, who have leased a house for residential purposes will be provided with a cash
grant of six months rental fee, and will be assisted in identifying alternative
accommodation.
14.        PAPs will also be provided compensation at full replacement cost for any other fixed
assets affected in part or in toto by the Project.



-130-
Annex 14
Page 7 of 22
15.       In cases where communuity infrastructure such as schools, factories, water sources, roads,
sewage systems or electrical supply is lost, this will be replaced at no cost to the community.
Section 4
People's Participation in the Project
16.        The PAPs will participate throughout the various stages of the resettlement activities.
They will be consulted by the competent authorities and will be invited to participate in public meetings
held by the respective PC and/or by the local peoples' committees.
17.        The PAPs will be adequately informed by the relevant local peoples' committees of the
details of the RAP.
Section 5
Baseline Information
A. Census and Inventory of Project Affected People
18.        Each RAP-2 will provide a census of families and persons affected by construction works
which will include an inventory of all losses incurred by each PAP.
19.        This information will include: (a) number, type, and area of the houses lost; (b) number,
quantity and area of all the residential plots lost; (c) number, category, type, and area of agricultural
land lost; and (d) quantity, category, and dimension of all other fixed assets affected by the Project.
B. Identification of Replacement Land and Cash Compensation
20.        Each RAP-2 will include information on the location, area, type, and category of the
replacement land available for residential and/or agricultural purposes and of the amount of cash
compensation to be provided, if that be the case.
C. The Socio-Economic Survey
21.        In addition to the PAPs census and inventory of affected properties, RAP-2 will also
include a socio-economic survey of the affected population, describing occupation and level of income
of the PAPs.



-13 1-
Annex 14
Page 8 of 22
Section 6
Implementation Arrangements
A. Schedule
22.        A detailed implementation schedule of the various resettlement activities to be undertaken
will be included in each RAP-2.
23.        Resettlement, land and cash compensation will be completed at least one month prior to
the scheduled start-up date of works in the respective Project site.
B. Compaints and Grievances
24.        Complaints and grievances related to any aspect of the RAP will be handled through
negotiations aimed at achieving consensus.
25.        Settlement between the PAP and local government will be first attempted at the level of
the Commune. If this first conciliation attempt fails, the case will be discussed a second time at the
District level. If at the District level the case is not resolved, an ad-hoc committee established by the
Provincial Peoples' Committee will decide the matter.
26.        In cases where, despite the above efforts, no agreement is reached between the parties, the
case will be submitted to the District court.
27.        PAPs who present their cases to the Commune, District and Provincial authorities, will be
exempted from any legal fees. PAPs, who bring their case to the District Court, will have to follow the
prevailing laws.
C. Supervision and Monitoring
28.        Implementation of RAP-2 will be regularly supervised and monitored by the respective PC
in coordination with the respective local peoples' committees. An agency nominated by each PC will
periodically carry out external monitoring and evaluation. External monitoring will be done by an
organization such as an academic or a research institution, an NGO or an independent consulting firm.
They will be identified and hired during the first year of Project implementation by each PC.
29.        Internal monitoring and supervision will:
(a)   verify that the census and socio-economic survey of all PAPs has been carried out and that
property assessment and compensation, resettlement and rehabilitation has been carried out
in accordance with the provisions of the RAP;
(b)   oversee that RAP is implemented as approved; and



-132-
Annex 14
Page 9 of 22
(c)  verify that funds for imnplementing the RAP are provided in a timely maner, are
sufficient for their purposes, and are spent in accordance with the provisions of the RAP.
30.       In addition to verifying the reports generated by the internal monitoring, the external
monitoring agency will carry out the following tasks:
(a)  evaluate the social and economic imnpact of RAP implementation on the PAPs;
(b)  verify if the objective of enhancement or at least restoration of income levels and
standards of living of the PAPs has been met; and
(c)  suggest modification in RAP implementation to achieve the principles and objectives set
forth in paragraph 7 of this RAP-1.
Setion 7
CosL and Budget
31.        Each RAP-2 will include detailed cost of resettlement, compensation and monitoring and
supervision with a breakdown by agricultural land, premise land, houses and other assets. The cost
estimates will make adequate provision for contingencies.

Section 1
Introduction
A. The Project
32.        The Power Sector Rehabilitation and Expansion Project (the Project) includes inter-alia
construction of 147 Iam, 220kv Krongbuk-Nhatrang power transmission line and 220kv terminal
substations at Krongbuk and Nhatrang (Part B.1 of the Project). This is the RAP for this project
component. The project also includes the rehabilitation and expansion of medium voltage (MV) and
low voltage (LV) electricity distribution networks, comprising construction of MV and LV lines
(overhead and underground) and MV/LV substations in Ho Chi Minh City (Part A. 1 of the Project) and
in Hue and Nhatrang (Part B. I of the Project) to be undertaken by the PC2 and PC3, respectively.
Regarding the latter, a separate Resettlement Action Plan has been prepared by PC3 and approved by
the Government of the Socialist Republic of Viet Nam, dated March 27, 1995.
B.   Transnission Resettlement Action Plan (RAP)
Introduction
1.         Under Part B.2 of the Project, Power Company 3 (PC3) will be constructing the 220kV,
147 klm, Krongbuk-Nhatrang transmission line (T/L) and the 220 kV terminal substations at Krongbuk
and Nhatrang. The width of the transmission Line Right of Way (ROW) is 22 meters.
Project Impact Area
2.         The project area is in west-central Viet Nam, in the central uplands where many ethnic
mninority groups reside. The line passes through sparsely populated areas of Dac Lac and Khanh Hoa
provinces, running south-east from Krongbuk substation through the gently sloping terrain around the
borders of Dac Lac and Khong Hoa provinces and traverses parts of the coastal plains near Nhatrang.
Protect Land Acquisition and Resettlement Impact
3.         Lands, houses, crops and other properties will be affected in the 22 meters ROW of the
transmission line. Out of the total T/L ROW area of 325 hectares only 3.56 hectares are actually
required for siting of the T/L towers. Waste land without any cultivation or houses on it will be
acquired for the Krongbuk and Nhatrang substations. The area affected by the Project includes 85
houses. About 51 % of ROW area is waste land under state control. About 157 hectares or 49 % of the
total land is cultivated. The major crops/trees in the T/L ROW are coffee, eucalyptus, rice, mango,
jackfruit, pineapple and vegetables. Of the 80 houses in the ROW, 66 houses are of good quality and
14 houses are made of thatched and other light materials. Table 1 summarizes the houses, crops, trees
and other properties affected by the project. Land which is not directly required for siting of the T/L
towers can be used for cultivation even after construction, however, trees above 4 meters in height will
not be allowed in the ROW.



-136-
Annex 14
Page 13 of 22
4.         This RAP has been prepared by the Power Company No. 3 (PC3) and approved by the
Government of the Socialist Republic of Viet Nam on March 27, 1995. It lays down the principles and
objectives, legal and institutional framework, modes of compensation and rehabilitation, peoples's
participation features and grievances procedures that will guide the resettlement and rehabilitation of the
project affected persons(PAPs). The RAP also includes results of the census and socio-economic survey
of the PAPs and properties to be affected, compensation and/or resettlement and rehabilitation
entitlements of various categories of PAPs; a timetable for implementation of the RAP; allocation of
the institutional responsibilities for implementation; a budget for funding the various compensation and
rehabilitation measures; and internal and external monitoring arrangements.
5.         The principle objective of this RAP is to ensure that all project affected persons (PAPs)
will be compensated and rehabilitated to assist them to improve, or at least maintain, their living
conditions and income earning capacity at the pre-Project levels. The RAP also aims to ensure that
communities are not broken up as a result of resettlement and that the PAPs are resettled in the vicinity
of their original residential areas. The project has been designed taking into consideration the need to
minimize resettlement. The route of the T/L has been chosen to ensure that it passes over minimum
number of houses and cultivated areas. No ethnic minority groups will be affected by the Project. Also
the lands chosen for substations is not under any productive use and does not have any built up
structures on it.
C. Project Affected People (PAPS)
6.          The PAPs include the following persons:
(a)   persons whose houses are in part or in toto affected by construction of the power
transmission line;
(b)   persons whose premise and/or agricultural land is in part or in toto affected (permanently
or temporarily) due to the construction of the power transmission line;
(c)   persons whose agricultural land is in the ROW of the power transmission line; and
(d)   persons whose businesses are affected in part or in toto (temporarily or permanently) due
the construction of the power transmission line.
D. Resettlement Principles and Objectives
7.         The principles outlined in the World Bank's Operational Directives 4.30 have been
adopted in preparing the RAP. In this regard the following principles and objectives have been applied:
(a)   Resettlement will be minimized as much as possible.
(b)   All PAPs residing or cultivating land in the Project area as of the date of the socio-
economic survey are entitled to compensation and/or resettlement.



-137-
Annex 14
Page 14 of 22
(c)   PAPs will be compensated, resettled and rehabilitated so as to improve their standard of
living or at least maintain their current standards at pre-Project level after resettlement;
(d)  The means of resettlement and rehabilitation are: compensation at replacement cost for
houses and other structures, agricultural land for land of equal productive capacity
acceptable to the PAP, replacement of premise land at least of equal size acceptable to the
PAP, transfer allowances, and compensation for trees and crops at market value.
(e)   Replacement premise and agricultural land will be as close as possible to the land that was
lost, acceptable to the PAP.
(f)   The resettlement transition period will be minimized and land for land and/or cash
compensation will be provided to the PAPs no later than one month prior to the scheduled
start-up date of construction at a given site.
(g)   Resettlement plans will be carried out following consultation with the PAPs.
(h)   The previous level of community services and resources will be maintained or improved
after resettlement.
(i)   Financial and physical resources for resettlement and rehabilitation will be made available
as and when required.
Institutional arrangements will ensure effective and timely design, planning and
implementation of the RAP.
(k)  Internal and external effective and timely monitoring will be provided on the
implementation of the RAP.
Section 2
Institutional and Legal Framework
A. Institutional Framework
8.         The responsibilities for implementing the RAP are as follows:
(a)   PC3 has overall responsibility for planning and implementing the RAP. For this purpose,
the PC2 will coordinate with the respective District Peoples Committees (DPCs). The
peoples committees at the commune level will discuss the various aspects of the RAP with
the PAPs.



-138-
Annex 14
Page 15 of 22
(b)   Funds for the resettlement program will be provided by PC3 based on decisions reached
through negotiations between local governments (district and conmmune peoples
committees) and the PAPs.
c)   PC3 will implement the RAP in coordination with the Provincial, District, and Commune
People's Committees.
B. Legal Framework
9.         The overall objective of the RAP is guided by Article 27 of the Land Law of 1993 (as
further amplified by Government Decree No 90-CP of 17th August 1994) enacted by the National
Assembly of the Socialist Republic of Viet Namn on July 1993. Article 27 provides that: "In case of
utmost necessity, when the State recovers land being used by a land user, for national defense, security,
national benefit, or public benefit purposes, the land user shall be given compensation for the
damages ".
10.        Compensation for land and fixed assets (e.g. houses) is defined by the Government Decree
No. 87-CP of the 17th of August 1994, which provides for land for land compensation and cash for
land, when land is not available, at rates established by Government. These rates have been established
for purposes of leasing government land, acquisition of land by government for national purposes, and
for tax value for issuing land use rights certificates.
Section 3
Entitlement Policy
11.        PAP will be entitled to the following types of compensation as they apply to individual
situations according to the eligibility and entitlement categories defined above.
PAPs losing agricultural land will be compensated as follows:
(a)  the general mechanism for compensation of lost agriculutural land will be through "land
for land" arrangements of equal productive capacity, satisfactory to the PAP. However, if
such land is not available in the vicinity, compensation in cash, at full replacement cost,
can be provided, as mutually agreed between the PAP and the relevant peoples'
committee. If the portion of the land to be lost represents 20% or less of the total area of
the land, cash compensation, at full replacement cost, will be provided to the PAP; and
(b)   PAPs who are forced to relocate or lose agricultural land shall be compensated with the
market price for the loss of standing crops. In case of loss of fruit or industrial trees,
these will be compensated at market price.
PAPs whose houses will be affected by the Project will be provided with:



-139-
Annex 14
Page 16 of 22
(c)  replacement residential (premises) land of equivalent size; and (ii) cash compensation,
reflecting full replacement cost of the structure without depreciation.
(d)  if the premise land and/or structure is only partially being affected by the Project and the
remaining part of the structure is habitable, either the entire premise land and structure
would be acquired from the PAP and compensation paid as under sub-paragraph (a), or
alternatively, compensation in cash reflecting full replacement cost of the portion of the
premise land and/or structure affected will be provided, as mutually agreed between the
PAP and the relevant peoples' committee; and
(e)   Transfer of Houses to New Sites: The PAP will be paid an allowance for transfer of
houses from their existing locations to the resettlement sites. The amount of assistance
will be 1 million VN Dong (about US $ 100), and may be increased for specific cases.
(f)   Land in T/L ROW: Land not directly acquired for construction but in the T/L ROW can
be used by the current users for cultivation, grazing and other activities, and will not be
compensated. However, a height restriction of 4 meters will be observed by the current
users for all future development. Hence, trees of commercial value with height more than
4 meters would be removed and fully compensated. Trees of non-commercial value
would be trimmed, and maintenance cost would be paid to the-owner, if he/she undertakes
this work.
(g)   Waste Land of LPCs: Arrangements for the use of waste lands belonging to the local
peoples' committees (LPCs) would be mutually agreed between the Government and the
concerned LPC.
(h)   Damage During Construction: Compensation would be paid for damage caused to crops
and trees during T/L construction at market rates.
Section 4
People's Participation in the Project
12.        The PAPs will participate throughout the various stages of the resettlement activities.
They will be consulted by the competent authorities and will be invited to participate in public meetings
held by the PC3 and/or by the local peoples' committees.
13.        The PAPs will be adequately informed by the relevant local peoples' committees of the
details of the RAP.
14.        All activities relating to fixing and payment of compensation and the resettlement program
will be carried out with the participation of the affected people and their representatives. The affected
communes and villages were informed about the project as soon as the proposal to implement the
project was finalized. The first activity to be carried out for implementation of the RAP, i.e.



-140-
Annex 14
Page 17 of 22
conducting surveys of the affected properties was carried out with the complete participation of the
affected person and peoples representatives. The survey record, prepared by district surveyors, was
finalized in the presence of the affected person, village head or his representative, commune
representative and a representative of PC3. The affected person signs the survey record if he is
satisfied with the details of his property recorded on the survey form. Fixation of compensation will be
similarly agreed to by the affected person. Land and property can only be acquired if the affected
person signs the compensation form. Land for resettlement will be approved by the commune before it
is selected for resettlement. Before finalization, various proposed sites will be shown to the affected
people and they select the location depending on their preference. In Vietnam there is time respected
tradition of consultations with and participation of the people in all matters which affect them. Most of
the activities mentioned in the RAP were and will be carried out with the involvement of the
conmnunes, which are truly representative of the peoples interests.
Section 5
Baseline Information
A. Cesus and Inventory of Project Affected People
15.        The physical survey of the selected route of the transmission line was carried out by the
Power Investigation and Design Company No. 2 (PIDC2), based at Nhatrang. The survey of affected
families and properties was done along with the detailed physical survey of the T/L route. The number
of houses and other properties affected, and the area under various agricultural, fruit and tree crops was
determined and plotted on the map providing the detailed physical description of the T/L route. The
precise location of each house and various cropped areas is given in this map. A list showing: (a) the
location of the affected houses and their position in the T/L ROW; (b) the type of materials used in
house construction; (c) the name of the owner and the exact number of affected persons in each house;
and (d) the income level of each household is given in Annex 1. In each of the affected houses resides
only one family; therefore, the total number of affected families is 80 (386 people). Agriculture, along
with raising of some animals, is the main occupation of the project affected persons (PAPs) .
16.        The lands proposed for construction of the Krongbuk and Nhatrang substations belong to
the local peoples' committees (LPCs). These are waste lands without any cultivation or houses or any
other economic activities being carried out on them.

Section 6
Implementation Arrangements
A. Resettlement and Construction Schedule
17.          The PAP  will be informed by project authorities and/or LPCs about the detailed
description of project impacts and the properties to be acquired at least 6 months before the start of
construction on the respective lands. Payment of compensation for crops, trees and other properties,
allotment of land for construction of relocated houses, and replacement land of equal productive
capacity, will be completed at least 1 month before construction starts on the affected area.
B. Implementation Arrangements
18.          Implementation of the R/C program  will be a joint effort of PC3, its subsidiary, Power
Transmission Utility (PTU) No. 2, the Provincial Peoples Committees (PPC), District Peoples'
Committees (DPC) and the commune authorities. The overall responsibility for implementing the RAP
will be that of PC3. PC3 will exercise its functions through two of its subsidiary agencies; namely the
PTU No. 2 based at Nhatrang and the Power Project Management Group based at Danang. Though
most of the activities will be carried out in close coordination with the Peoples' Committees at various
levels, the officials of PC3 and its two subsidiaries will ensure that implementation complies with the
RAP. PC3 will be responsible for coordinating the disbursement of funds. The funds would be
disbursed to the people directly by PTU No. 2, with the LPC acting as a witness.



-142-
Annex 14
Page 19 of 22
19.          The PPCs of the respective provinces will inform  the concerned districts about the
resettlement program and direct them to take the steps necessary for compensation and resettlement of
the PAP within their jurisdiction. The DPCs will inform the PAP and the respective communes about
the project and the RIC program and coordinate its activities. The DPCs will be responsible for fixing
compensation levels for various types of affected properties in accordance with the principles of this
RAP (see legal framework) and supervise the detailed surveys of these properties. Payment of
compensation will be supervised by PC3 and its agencies and allotment of alternative lands will be the
responsibility of the DPCs. The commnune authorities will be in charge of informing the PAPs about
the project impact and implementation schedule, to redress their grievances and to act as a
communication link between the PAPs and the DPCs, PPCs, PTU No. 2 and PC3. Most routine
activities will be coordinated directly by the conmmune and district authorities. PC3 will finance the
total cost of the RAP and ensure the timely availability of funds. Table 2 shows the activities which
need to be carried out as a part of the R/C program and the organization(s) responsible for it.
C. Implementation Schedule
20.          Table 3 shows the implementation schedule of the RAP activities.  A  Chart of the
implementation schedule is given in Annex 2.

D. Complaints and Grievances
21.          Complaints and grievances related to any aspect of the RAP will be handled through
negotiations aimed at achieving consensus.
22.          Settlement between the PAP and local government will be first attempted at the level of
the Commune. If this first conciliation attempt fails, the case will be discussed a second time at the
District level. If at the District level the case is not resolved, an ad-hoc committee established by the
Provincial Peoples' Cormmittee will decide the matter.
23.          In cases where, despite the above efforts, no agreement is reached between the parties, the
case will be submitted to the District court.
24.          PAPs who present their cases to the Commune, District and Provincial authorities, will be
exempted from any legal fees. PAPs, who bring their case to the District Court, will have to follow the
prevailing laws.
E. Supervsion and Monitoring
25.          Implementation of the RAP will be regularly supervised and monitored by PC3 in
coordination with the respective local peoples' committees. An agency nominated by each PC will
periodically carry out external monitoring and evaluation. External monitoring will be done by an
organization such as an academic or a research institution, an NGO or an independent consulting firm.
They will be identified and hired during the first year of Project implementation by each PC.



-144-
Annex 14
Page 21 of 22
26.        Internal monitoring and supervision will:
(a)   verify that the census and socio-economic survey of all PAPs has been carried out and that
property assessment and compensation, resettlement and rehabilitation has been carried out
in accordance with the provisions of the RAP;
(b)   oversee that RAP is implemented as approved; and
(c)   verify that funds for implementing the RAP are provided in a timely manner, are
sufficient for their purposes, and are spent in accordance with the provisions of the RAP.
27.        In addition to verifying the reports generated by the internal monitoring, the external
monitoring agency will carry out the following tasks:
(a)   evaluate the social and economic impact of RAP implementation on the PAPs;
(b)   verify if the objective of enhancement or at least restoration of income levels and
standards of living of the PAPs has been met; and
(c)   suggest modification in RAP implementation to achieve the principles and objectives set
forth in of this RAP.
Section 7

A. Budget for RAP activities
28.        Timely availability of funds for carrying out surveys, payment of compensation, allotment
of alternative sites and transfer of houses to new sites is crucial for effective implementation of the
RAP. It is the responsibility of PC3 to ensure that adequate funds for implementing the RAP are
available on schedule. Table 4 provides an estimate of the RAP costs.

Summary of Mitigation Measures S-
2.            In order to reduce environmental impacts from  the proposed development, mitigation
measures, summarized below, have already been put in hand in relation to (a) altering the location for
the cooling water discharge point and (b) agreeing adequate compensation for the acquisition of land
from a local shrimp farm cooperative. As described below, mitigation measures are also planned to
reduce the impacts of noise and waste water streams. Apart from these, and taking into account the
relatively minor residual impacts of the proposed development no further mitigation measures are
considered necessary.
3.            The initially selected cooling water discharge point, which was beside the power station,
has been relocated to a more suitable site because of the danger of unacceptably high temperature rises
in the receiving waters. This will require the construction of a 3 km long pipe route to the new
discharge point which is located by a large body of water where the discharge of the cooling water will
have no significant impact. While the laying of this pipeline will itself cause some loss of mangrove
trees, the route will be chosen to minimize this impact and, as the pipe is buried underground, any
disturbed area will after a few years return to its original state. Planting of any disturbed areas will
reduce the time for regrowth.
1/ Paras. 2, 3 and 4 are not relevant to cooling tower alternative.



-148-
Annex 15
Page 3 of 3
4.         For the development of the proposed cooling water intake lagoon. PC2 will need to
acquire 40 hectares of land currently used for shrimp and rice farming. Adequate compensation terms
have been agreed which will allow the owners to move their activities to areas not currently utilized and
avoid socio-economic impacts as well as any indirect environmental effects.
5.         Available data on existing noise at the site are limited, but indicate that there may be a
danger of breaching guideline levels at nearby residences. A survey to be carried out will give a much
better picture of the present situation. If this survey shows that guidelines are being breached then it
may be necessary to specify the level of acoustic cladding and other silencing equipment for the new
development such that it will have no significant additional noise at the site perimeter. Given that the
waste heat boilers and steam turbines will be enclosed, the cost of the additional acoustic insulation
would be very small compared with the overall project cost.
6.         Depending on the outcome of the survey findings two alternative noise mitigation measures
may be more economic. These are (a) the erection at the site perimeter of a berm (earth mound) with
planted trees and shrubs to insulate noise emissions and (b) the acoustic insulation of residences where
indoor noise is high. The costs associated with both these mitigation measures are minor.
7.         Waste water streams from the proposed development includifig (a) water plant treatment
waste, (b) sewage, (c) surface drains, (d) boiler blowdown, (e) boiler acid cleaning effluent will all be
reated, as required, so that the effluent discharged satisfies Vietnamese waste water effluent regulations
and will cause no significant impact.

VIET NAM
Power Sector Rehabilitation and Expansion Project
Assumptions in the Financial Statements
Inflation
1.         Viet Nam's inflation rate over the past years has been volatile as the country was
undergoing its adjustment process toward a market-oriented economy. The inflation rate was 68% in
1990 and 1991 declining to 18% in 1992 and 8% in 1993. The Government is keen on maintaining a
single-digit inflation rate. The Bank expects the rate of inflation to drop further and, on average, to
stabilize around 5-6% per annum during the projected period 1994-2000. Unless otherwise stated, a
5% inflation rate has been built into the financial projections.
Tariffs
2.         The financial projections assume that tariffs would be progressively raised to an average
level of US cents 7/kWh by 1999 as proposed by the Government. Assuming a 5 % annual depreciation
of the Dong vis-a-vis the dollar, this tariff in 1999 would be about US cents 974/kWh for PC2 and US
cents 848/kWh for PC3.
Losses
3.         Technical and non-technical losses currently at 20% and 3% for PC2 and 18% and 7% for
PC3, respectively, are: (a) projected to be maintained at 19% and 3% for PC2; and (b) projected to be
reduced to 17% and 6% in 1998 and to drop further to 17% and 5% in 2000 for PC3, in line with
Govermnent's proposals.
Purchase of Power
4.         The projected price of purchased power for PC2 of about D 290 per kWh sold is based on
the estimated cost of a medium-sized hydroelectric station. Currently, PCI and PC2 sell power to PC3
at D 5/kWh. This negligible tariff was set by the Government to improve PC3's financial results
without adversely affecting the finances of PC1 and PC2. As PC3's financial condition continues to
remain unsatisfactory till around 1998, the projections assume that the purchase price would continue to
remain at D 5/kWh.
Cost of Fuel
5.         Fuel includes the cost of oil, gas and diesel consumed by PC2 and PC3 in their thermal
generating facilities. All fuel costs have been assumed at their present prices until 1995 when prices are
projected to increase by 10% each in 1996, 1998 and 2000. These expenses are based on fuel prices
used in the calculation of the present tariff structure as follows:



-159-
Annex 20
Page 2 of 3
Power Company No. 2
Oil. The price of heavy oil including average transportation cost to site is at present D
1,324,250/MT. This price is about equal to US$18 - US$19 per barrel. PC2 is permitted to
negotiate the price with the oil companies. On average, the steam stations of PC2 use 0.25 kg of
oil/kWh. The fuel cost per kWh produced is D 331.
Gas. It is assumed that starting 1996 natural gas will be available for power generation although
the price has not yet been decided. It is expected that the price will be between US$ 2.00 (D
21,800) and US$ 2.50 (D 27,250)/MMBTU (252,000 kcal). The financial projections assume a
price of US$ 2.00 per 252,000 kcal.
Diesel. The price of diesel is at present D 2,635,250/MT (US$ 241.77fMT or about D 2,725
per liter). Diesel stations use on average 0.2 kg/kWh produced.
Power Companv No. 3
Apart from a few micro hydro stations, PC3 operates only diesel stations at the following cost on
average: D 2,800/kg plus 0.5% for losses during transport and D 145/kg for transport. Diesel
stations use on average 0.272 kg/kWh produced. The price is negotiable and was decreased by
D 30 from the above price in July 1, 1994.
Salaijes, Wages and Benefits
6.         PC2 and PC3 record only base salaries and wages in their income staternents; staff,
however, also draws bonuses and benefits which are not recorded in the costs of the income statement.
The projections include bonuses and benefits in the income statements.
Operation, Maintenance and Administration
7.         PC2 and PC3 are required to eliminate the cost component "Facility Maintenance" from
their income statements; these expenses have been included in the projections.
Taxes
8.         Taxes are based on current levels as follows: (a) Tax on Revenues at 8% of revenues and
4% of other revenues; (b) Charge on Natural Resources at 2% of that part of revenues from sales of
power which corresponds to the percentage of hydro generation versus total generation; (c) Tax on
Capital at 2.4% of net plant in service; and (d) Income Tax at 25%.
Depreciation
9.         Depreciation rates for PC2 and PC3 are prescribed by the Government and calculated on
the following basis: turbines (8%), rockfill dams (2%), concrete dams (3%), distribution systems
(8.5%). The financial projections include depreciation, on average at the rate of 5.4% for PC2 and
5.0% for PC3.



-160-
Annex 20
Page 3 of 3
Capital Structure
10.        The following capital structure is assumed: (a) existing Government capital remains as
equity and is not transformed into debt; (b) starting FY94 new investments are assumed to be financed
at one third Government contributions and two thirds debt; (c) long term debts have been assumed at an
annual interest rate of 7.5% with repayment terms of up to 15 years including two years of grace; (d)
no dividend payments on equity have been assumed; and (e) PC2 and PC3 will capitalize interest during
construction.
Investments
11.        Projected capital expenditures are those estimnated to provide the additonal plant and
equipment required to meet the demand forecast, escalated at the rate of expected inflation of 6% p.a.
Fixed Assets
12.        Due to doubtful past valuation procedures, fixed assets as recorded by PC2 and PC3 may
not represent their real value. Consequently, the financial projections are based on fixed assets as
available at the end of FY93.
Current Assets and Liabilities
13.        Accounts receivable are projected to be approximately two months and four months of
revenues for PC2 and PC3, respectively. Current payables are projected at the equivalent of one week
of fuel expenses and 20% of annual capital expenditures.

VIET NAM
Power Sector Rehabilitation and Expansion Project
Economnic Justification of the Project
1.         This Annex presents the assumptions and working details for the economic justification of
the project components.
Basis for Costs and Monetary Benefits
2.          All costs and monetary benefits are converted to 1994 prices. It is common practice to
apply a shadow exchange rate multiplier and a conversion factor for expenditure on local labor. The
former is used to correct for distortions in the exchange rate; because of the liberalized nature of the
market for foreign exchange in Viet Nam, it is estimated that the exchange rate does not suffer from
distortions, and no adjustments are made. For the latter, designed to remove distortions of subsidies
and taxes from this component, a conversion factor of 0.75 is assumed.
Conversion of Ba Ria Open Cyde Turbines to Combined Cycle Operation
3.         The power balance for PC2's system is shown in Table 3.1 indicating the need for
additional capacity by 1996-97. Given the shape of PC2's daily load curve, and the energy inflows to,
storage capacity and power capability of the hydro stations in PC2's service area, the requirement is for
base load rather than peaking capacity.
4.          With the availability of offshore natural gas at about US$ 2.0 per MMBTU (economic cost
about US$1.3/MMBTU) by mnid 1995, Ba Ria becomes the least cost proposition for base load thermal
capacity addition in PC2's system by 1996-97. There are three basic natural gas-fired options for the
expansion of Ba Ria's generating capacity. These options and the levelised costs for each are shown in
Table A21.1 below. The least-cost solution is that proposed for the project: the conversion of three gas
turbines to a combined cycle block. The conversion of existing turbines to combined cycle operation
does not require additional fuel; however, the construction of new plant will require this fuel.
TABLE A21.1: Comparison of Options For Expanding Capacity at Ba Ria
Option                  | Combined Cyde | Gas Turbine Plant  Steam Turbine
Plant                     I   Addition
Investment Cost (US$/kW)                               800              550           1,300
Fixed 0 & M Cost (US$/kW p. a.)                          8               104
Variable 0 & M Cost (USc/kWh)                          0.15            0.20            0.05
Heat Rate (BTU/kWh)                                   8,000           12,000             0
Levelised Cost (US c/kWh), Plant Factor-70%                                                l
Gas Price: $2/MMBTU, Discount Rate-10%                 3.41            3.82            2.61
Gas Cost: $1.3MNMBTU, Discount Rate-10%                2.85            2.98            2.61
Gas Cost: $1.3/MTU. Discount Rate-13.5%                3.23            3.24            3.23

Estimation of the EIRR of The Project
5.          Assumptions regarding the project are:
(a)   the capital costs are US$62.82 million in foreign costs and US$6.26 million in local costs;
this represents the base costs plus a 10% allowance for physical contingencies; price
contingencies are excluded; this also excludes duties and taxes; 26% of the local costs
represent expenditure on labor;
(b)   capital expenditure is phased 40% in 1995, 40%in 1996 and 20% in 1997;
(c)   O&M  costs are assumed to be US$1.73 million per year of operation, in real terms
(approximately 2.5% of capital expenditure);
(d)   no fuel costs are attributed to the project; the addition of the steam unit increases output
simply by recycling the exhaust gases from turbine operation;
(e)  the unit operates at a 50% plant load factor in 1997, followed by a 68% plant load factor
thereafter; the unit has a 20 year life, and ceases operation in 2016;
(f)  the output from the unit is decreased by the level of losses forec:ast for the system in each
year of operation; this represents the incremental sales from the project;
(g)   the tariff is assumed to increase progressively to 7 USc/kWh by 1999, in nominal terms;
based on Governments proposals.
6.          Table A21.6 presents the computation of incremental benefits and costs attributed to the
project, while Table A21.2. presents the results of the computation for the Base Case and various
sensitivity cases.
TABLE A21.2: Economic Internal Rate of Return for Ba Ria Project

Rehabilitation of the Distribution Network in HCMC, Hue and Nhatrang
7.          Tables A21.3, A21.4 and A21.5 present: (a) capital expenditures on the distribution and
upstream sub-transmission systems; (b) technical losses; (c) electricity sales; (d) energy required by the
system; and (e) unserved energy, for the "with project" and "without project" cases, for HCMC, Hue
and Nhatrang. The capital costs include a 10% allowance for physical contingency; price contingencies

are excluded as also are duties and taxes. Of the local expenditure, 26% is in the form of labor
services. No incremental O&M costs were included for either case; O&M costs would be even higher
for the "without project" case.
8.         The EIRRs are calculated on the stream of costs and benefits over a project economic life
of 25 years. The losses (technical only) are valued at the LRMC figure of 5 USc/kWh at the
subtransmission level and the reduction in unsupplied energy is conservatively valued at 10 times the
tariff. The details of the cost and benefit streams are presented in Tables A21.7 - A21.9. EIRRs
calculated for the base and several sensitivity cases are tabulated below. The sensitivities undertaken
are designed to examine the impact of: (i) increasing capital costs; (ii) lower demand; and (iii) a 50%

Energy GWh                    2869       3539       4401       5463      6774       8434      10401
Load Dispatch Centers
9.           The project benefits are quantified over the period to 2012, providing a 15 year period for
benefits following commissioning. It is assumed that the control centers would allow a 0.5 % saving in
energy efficiency; given the energy constrained nature of the system in the medium term, this is
considered analogous to an increase in sales and is therefore valued using the prevailing tariff rate,
adjusted for losses. The value of unserved energy used is assumed conservatively at ten times the tariff
level; the quantity of unserved energy due to transmission faults is estimated to be half the total
unserved energy forecast. It is assumed that the control centers could provide a 20% reduction in the
unserved energy (declining from 1.7% in 1994 to 0.5% by 2001) due to transmission faults. It is also
assumed that by 2012, the improved frequency control would have lead to a reduction in UPS
equipment in the country equivalent to 0.1 % of forecast peak demand. This equipment costs in the
region of US$2,000 per kW. Finally, it is assumed that automation would save about 35 staff valued at
US$5,000 per staff-year.
10.          The investment in the load dispatch centers totals US$38.75 million; annual O&M  costs
equal to 2% of this expenditure are assumed. The investment is estimated to be phased 20%, 40%,
40% over the years 1995-1997.
11.          The EIRR (see Table A21. 10 for details), including all benefits, is 27.0%. Decreasing by
50% the benefits from a reduction in unserved energy and in the purchase of UPS equipment gives an
EIRR of 20.3%, and assuming that efficiency savings are equal to 0.25% of generation reduces the
EIRR to 23.3%. Taking the improvement in efficiency alone, the EIRR is 11 %.
